O, sons, for I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, by the completion of it the end is achieved in it, and by the expositions of it, and by the declarations of it, it is my view that you complete it with this treatise, which is part of the operation with me, that is, surgery.
Because the operation with me is prostrate in our region and in our time entirely private, while many risk the science of it, and its vestiges are held captive; and there remain of it only some small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have been altered and have become subject to those errors and uncertainties because their clauses the understandings of it and are elongated the force of it and the art.
And it is seen to me that you bring that to life with the order of this treatise in that according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and for that it may come with the forms of the tools of cautery and of the other instruments of the work as it is by addition of the declaration, and by preparation of it, which cause is necessary.
But the cause for which no one has been found a good artificer with his hand in this our time, is because the art of medicine is long, and that it requires the actor to be exercised before it in the science of anatomy, which reconciles Gualia because it knows the joints of the members and the forms of those, and the conjunction and separation of them; and to have the knowledge of the bones, the nerves and the tendons, the number of those, and the egress of them; and of the pulsating veins and the quiet ones, and of the places of the emergence of them.
And for that reason, Hippocrates says that with a name is little, but in the work much, and most of all in the art of the hand.
But now we have already said that in the introduction of this book; for whoever is not learned in that which we have said of anatomy, is not evacuated that he will not fall into error for which many men die, as I have seen too many of those, who some are formed in this science and throw themselves from that their science and their experience.
For I saw a foolish and inexperienced physician who had incised an abscess scrophilos in the neck of a woman, and incised some arteries of the neck so that great blood flowed while the woman died among the hands of him.
And I saw another physician who prescribed that the trachea of a man who had been processed in his state, and the stone was large, and it came to him and extracted that stone with a piece of the bladder, so that that man on the third day died.
And I had already been called to extract that, and I saw that because of the greatness of the stone and because of the disposition of the patient, I knew on him that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was taking a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and he came to a black crusted man who was broken in his hip; and prepared the physician with his ignorance, extracted the fracture, over the wound, with splints and splints with strong structure, and did not leave the wound to breathe.
And then he dissolved it according to his desires, and then he ligated it, and then he left it for some days and commanded that we untie the ligament; and thus it came to be that the hip and the leg became inflamed, and it came to ruin.
And I was called to him, and I prepared to untie the ligament, and achieved tranquility and then eased his pains.
But however, already corruption was confirmed in the limb, so that I could not restrain it, and did not cease to wander the corruption in the limb until the patient perished.
And I saw another physician who perforated a cancerous abscess, and it was ulcerated after some days, until the malignancy of it was magnified in its lord.
The cause of which is that the cancer is pure of melancholic humor, so that it does not come to it with iron at all, but that it be in a limb which suffers that it be held captive by all.
And for that reason, sons, it is necessary for you that the operation with me be devised in two divisions: that is, in operation to which health is associated, and in work with which there is peril in the major dispositions.
And I have already insisted on this in all places of this book in which I bring operation in which there is error and fear; for it is necessary for you to guard this and leave that, so that the foolish ones do not find a way to speak and to dishonor you.
And therefore, take your weapons with diligence and with the protection of God, and your patients with facility and with firmness.
And use the best way by the grace of God, seeking health and praiseworthy success, and leave the terrible illnesses of difficult healing, and hold your weapons from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation in your faith and in your name does not escape you: for more is it remaining to your glory, and more in the world and in the end to your sanctitates.
Gualia already said in some of his monitions: "Do not treat a bad illness, so that bad physicians are not called by name."
And now I have divided this book according to three chapters.
Begins the division of the book, and the first of the first part. The first chapter ordered from the head to the feet, in the forms of the instruments and in the tools of the cauteries, and of that which is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, of incision and perforation, and of cupping glasses, and of leeches, and of the extraction of arrows and of things similar to those, all chaptered and ordered by the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, of restoration and dislocation, and of the cure of sprains and of things similar to those; chapter ordered from the head to the feet, and of the forms of the instruments.
It is necessary that I say the quality of the judgments of that cautery and of its harms, and in what cases it is prohibited cauterization.
Therefore I say that the sermon of the quality of the judgment of cauterization and of its harm is a long and prolix sermon, and subtle by science, and secretly hidden; and already many wise men have spoken of it, and they have disagreed, and to me a little of their sermons suffices, fearing prolixity.
And therefore I say that cauterization is harmful to all cases universally, which are in matter or are matter, except for two cases, which are cases of matter that is hot.
In the case of a hot and dry matter, they disagree; for some say that cauterization is beneficial to that, and others say the contrary of that, that cauterization is not suitable for illness which is by quality and by dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inconvenient that illness hot and dry with that which is hot and dry be cured.
And those who say the contrary of that, say that cauterization is made beneficial in all hot and dry illnesses that come in the bodies of men, because when you compare the body of man and its humors to the nature of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I say for the sermon of that, that experience has already taught me some times.
But however, it is not necessary that it should come upon this that which has already been explored and exercised in the chapter of cauterization by previous exercise, and who has known the diversity of the constitution of men and the disposition of the illnesses in their own bodies, and the causes of those, and their accidents, and the duration of those.
But in the other cases, there is no fear for you, and more so in the hot and humid illnesses, because already all the physicians have agreed upon those, and they are not disagreed upon the judgment with cauterization in those.
And know, children, that of the secret of curing by cauterization with fire and of its goodness, it is because fire is simple, the action of which does not reach beyond the member which is cauterized and does not reach the other member attached to it except with a small harm.
But the action of burning medicine reaches that in the members which are farther from it, and greatly causes to come in the member illness of difficult healing and greatly harms.
But fire, because of its sublimity and of the goodness of its substance, does not do anything but that which is superfluous, and it is already known to us by experience and by the length of service of study in the art about the truth of the causes; and for that reason I am excused for the length of the sermon, and if it were not that it is not written in my book in this place to you the secret hidden with fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies and of its expulsion by which expels the illnesses, with a philosophical and demonstrative sermon, which would be acute in your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree about the time in which it is convenient to make cauterization and they pause the best time of spring.
And I say that cauterization is convenient at all times, because so that the harm by the accidental time is submerged in the benefit of that which with the cauterization is aimed, and more so if the cauterization is for pains or of necessary pains, strong and fistulous, which do not suffer delay because it is feared of those that come malice, which is greater than a small harm entering by time.
And therefore do not catch in your minds, o, children, that this is not esteemed but by the vulgar people and the foolish physicians, because it is that to that illness that is cured by cauterization it is not reduced all times, and they pause that consequence.
And the cause is not at all like that which they think about it, because cauterization is not but in place of medicine which alters the constitution and dries the humors which are the cause for which the pains come.
But however, cauterization is superfluous over medicine by the will of its value and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that its illness may return at some time in the future, according to the constitution of the patient and the location of its illness, and its virtue, and what is prepared in the body of it of the addition of superfluities in it, and what has reached it in its acquisition in foods and things similar to those causes; unless that illness in which cauterization is administered is a subtle illness in a member of few superfluities and humors, as cauterization of teeth for pain and things similar to that, it is possible that in it that pain does not return, but rather that it is made in small.
And more common speech is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is right speech, not that I understand it in it, because I believe that there is no cure that profits with medicine nor with any other cause except cautery.
And the cause is contrary to that; and the understanding that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is only when they administer the ways of healing in some diseases, and those medicines do not confer, and then at the end of the cause man administers cautery, and it profits to that. And therefore it is said that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the understanding which I understand the common people and many foolish doctors.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not make a scar, as it is not absolutely true, because I have already seen it and have found that it does not do so except in some bodies where others do not, and cautery with that is good and better than with iron as they said; however, when you do cautery with fire with gold, it is not declared to you, because it is ignited according to the quantity that you want for the roar of the gold, and that it prepares to receive the heat; and if you adjust over it fire, the gold melts for the fire, and in the fire some sheets so that the artisan catches for the occupation of that.
And for that reason cautery with iron must be done more lightly and more carefully to the rectitude of operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter on cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head among the feet, so that afterwards the one who asks for it may have what they want from it.
The first chapter.
This cauterization confers to the humidity and coldness over the  servant accident of which there are two causes, so it is the cause of soda and multitude of fluxes rheumatic, called corissa, from the head to the parts of the eyebrows and ears flow, and multitude of sleep, and pain of teeth and of the goiter, and universally of all sickness that comes by coldness, as well as paralytically, soda and apoplexy, and similar in those diseases.
The form of this cauterization is this, that first you command the patient to be evacuated with laxative medicine the head modifying, for three or for four nights, according to that requires the virtue of the patient and the age of him and his custom.
And then command him to shave his head, and then do that seizure between your hands on a bench lowered and that he place his hands on his feet.
And then place the razor of your palm near the nose between his eyebrows. But however, as the your said of the middle place is reached, sign that place with a tenta, and then ignite the cautery olive of which this is the form:
And then place that on the place signed with a tenta, in the manner that descends, with which your hand be constricted little by little, and you revolve that.
And then lift your hand slightly and look at the place, and if you see already of the bone being discovered any quantity of the head, as the quantity of a grain of er, then raise your hand, and if not return your hand with that iron, with another of that, if it is cooled, until it is seen of the bone that I have told you.
And then take a little salt and dissolve that on the place and leave that for three days.
And then place on it a poultice soaked in butter and leave that on it until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the place with ointment tetrafarmacon until it is healed.
And already they said that when the plague remains open, so much better gets the scar, because it is better and more helpful.
And they said some of them that the spine should be cauterized into the bone, and that the cautery should be kept until some part of the surface of the bone is burned.
And then scrape that which is burned of the bone, and then be cured.
And they said others that with the cautery it should reach the end, until it presses into the bone strong pressure until the bone breaks, and this is the form of alphecati small: And they estimate of that place expire the vapors of the head.
And it should be kept open for a long time, and then be cured until it is consolidated.
But to me, these two species of cautery have not been seen at all, except in some men according to their way of fear; and leave that, of me, it is better for health, when it is; because the head is revealed by the solution of continuity of it as we have testified in the other members, and more so when the head of the patient is of a cold nature.
And the species of cautery first is more safe and better of me; and of that I use and with that work with health.
Second chapter.
Of the cautery of the head.
When chronic and long-lasting pain occurs throughout the head and is prolonged in the patient, and use of herbs, poultices, and capipulges, and plasters, and guats, and cadels, and gualinas, and semblances, and mostly if it has already been cauterized with a cautery that is recounted and does not benefit him from any of those causes, then consider that if the head of the patient is of strong creation in its nature; and is not frail and finds a great deal of heat, then cauterize it with another cautery besides that one a little. And then cauterize that over the horn of his head with a cautery until the bone is parted. Incise the bone and uncover the quantity which we have recounted and cauterize that with a cautery in the back part of the head in the place which is called vas, — and that is the place in which a leech is placed. And alleviate your hand in this, and do not uncover the bone, because the patient by this suffers a great deal of pain different from the pain of all the other cauteries of the head.
And I say this cautery in its place, because whoever cauterizes with the cautery with which the horns of the head and the occiput are cauterized, is more subtle than that with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is the form of it.
Chapter Three.
Of cauterization of  non-ancient hernia.
When pain in the side of the head occurs, or pain is extended into the eye, it is evacuated with medicines that modify the head, and another cure is administered, which I have said in the divisions of the diseases; and if none of this is helpful, then cauterization in it is in two ways: either cauterization with acute and burning medicine, or with iron.
But cauterization with burning medicine is that you take a piece of alum, and scrape it and separate the extremities of it from both ends. And then incise the place of the pain in the temple with a sharp lancet until there is a place made in it below the bone, until it is hidden.
And then strengthen over it with a stopped constriction, and leave it for the space of three hours; and then untie it and take away the alum, and leave the wound for two or three days, and then place over it a poultice submerged in butter until the place makes a scab.
And then cure this with a gargle until it is healed.
And if you wish, do this with some burning medicines which I have written in the two treatises of burning medicines.
But cauterization with iron according to this manner: ignite a cautery of which this is the form:
and it is called a clavilh, because the head of it is as shaped as a clove in which there is some curvature, and in the middle part of it is a small eminence.
And then place over the place of the pain, and keep your hand — so that the artery which is below is not burned — and revolve the iron little by little with speed.
And if the quantity of it which is burned by the sharpness of the bone is so much that most of it, then remove your hand so that the artery which is below is not burned, so that there does not come a flow of blood.
And then imbibe a poultice in salt water and place it over the place, and leave it for three days; and then place a poultice ground with butter, and then cure with a gargle until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize with the extremity of the cutellary according to the cautery, and guard yourself from incision of the artery in this hernia properly non-ancient.
Chapter Four.
Of cauterization of ancient hernia.
When you cure a hernia with that which we have said of the previous cure, and that which we have said in the divisions of the diseases, and if none of the cure is helpful, and sometimes because of the illness that does not suffice for it that which we have said of the first cauterization with medicine or of the cauterization with fire, then it is that you ignite the cutellary cautery until it is white-hot, because it signifies over the place of the pain with a line of length of which most of it, or whichever one; and remove your hand for a moment and strengthen that before you incise the artery and reach until the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to guard against the continuation of the mandible, which is harmful to chewing, and that the muscle be not burned and the nerve which feels that, and that it does not become a spasm.
And if it is about the custody and caution of the flow of blood from the artery that is incised, because in the incision of it there is fear, and more so to him who ignores what is done and is not studious and experienced; and leaves the operation in it at the beginning.
And I will come with a remembrance of the regiment of the flow of blood accidents of the artery according to its manner, in its place in this book.
And if you see of this illness that this cautery does not suffice and you see the body of the patient tolerable, cauterize that in the middle part of the head as we have recounted, and cure the wound until it is healed.
And if you are, administer the cautery which we have mentioned in the chapter of the cautery having two handles, and this cauterization is better and more convenient.
Chapter V.
Of cauterization of ear pains.
When in the ear there is pain from heat and it is cured with laxative causes and with the other cure which I have said in the division, and the pain is not removed, then ignite the cautery, and this is the one which has a point, of which this is the form:
And when you point it to the ignition, and it is moved around the entire ear as a wheel is rolled, or in the circuit of whichever part if the pain is in whichever. Lengthen it with the cautery from the root of the ear little by little as if you were feeling the place with your finger.
And if the cautery of ten points in the entire ear, and that one, and then cure the places while they are healing.
Chapter VI.
Of cauterization of tumors.
A tumor which is cured and by cauterization is only of the kinds which come from phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of the diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the kind that arises from dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that kind of tumor with leeches and purgatives and washes, and if you do not find comfort in your cure, then you should cauterize the tumor with three cauteries: the first at the root of the ear, the second a little below its temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And pause your cautery for the opposite of the diseased part, because softening does not come except in the part that is healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize that with the cautery in the right of the extremity of the ear, as sovereign a little above the corner of the head, and in the temple another, the length of which should be according to the length of the finger, and rest your hand with the cautery until the quantity of the majority of the species of the cord is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a species of the cutler, the form of which is oppositely placed. But however, more subtle is that one a little as if you were seeing; and where the handle in it of superfluous thickness a little.
And then cure the place with that which is oppositely proceeded until it is healed.
Chapter VII.
Of cauterization of old apoplexy.
When apoplexy is old and you cure that with the water which we have said and you do not find comfort in your medication and the malady has no fever, then cauterize that with four cauteries: above all the horns of its head; and with cautery and the middle place of the head, as we have said; and with cautery in the groin. And the manner of the cautery is made according to what has been said.
And already it is cauterized above the mouth of the stomach; and it is more behind; and then it should be cured with the water which proceeds.
Chapter VIII.
Of cauterization of oblivion made by phlegm.
And if they should be given to the patient at the beginning leeches large and pills the service modifying.
And then shave the head of the whole patient and place on the groin of him a plaster of cente described in the treatise of the plasters.
And place that some times, for that is the manner of cauterization. And do water according to that same order which I have already said.
And therefore, if by those he is healed, well; and if not, then make to him three cauteries in the rear part of his head, which are descending from the most sovereign part of the head into the part more below the neck. Chapter IX.
Of cauterization of paralysis and of softening of the whole body.
And that you proceed in the modification of the head with leeches and with the water which we have said; and then shave the head of the patient, and then cauterize that with the cautery in the middle place of the head, and with cautery above all the horns of the head, and with cautery above the rear part of it, and with three cauteries upon the vertebrae of the neck.

And then take care of the one inside that is healing, and this cauterize with olive oil.
Chapter X.
Of cauterization of epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, but epilepsy is from phlegm.
And therefore, whoever modifies the brain of him at the beginning with years and with the other cure which we have said in the division when the patient is great and is tolerating the excess of medicines.
And if it is a child who does not suffer the medicines, then administer  guarguarsmes and masticators to the servant brain, before that for a few days, with the blessing of the foods.
And then shave the head of the patient, and then cauterize that with a cautery in the middle location of the head according to the previous manner, and with another cautery in the nape of his neck, and on each horn of his head cauterize. And if the patient is strong and is tolerating, then cauterize that with cauteries the ones which I have said, having paralytically and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
And cauterize with olive oil according to what is preceded.
But if the patient is a child, then pause cauterization subtle according to this manner.
Chapter XI.
Of cauterization of melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are humidities corrupted and phlegm thick, then cauterize that with the cauteries which we have said in the having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is superfluity declining to melancholy, and the body of the patient is humid, then give him to drink water that purifies the brain of him according to what has preceded in the division.
And then shave the head of the patient, and then make a proper torc of him over the circle, and then place that in the middle location of the head.
And the patient be felt to be cauterized, and be held from all parts.
And then apply liniment; and it is more worthy of bordering with wool of sheep. And warm that over the fire for temperate heating by measure, the one which the said suffers when it is most in him. And then put that in the middle location of the head of him in the circle, and let him inside that it is cooled.

And then apply that coat embedded in wool or in gray of guinea.
Chapter XII.
Of cauterization of water descending in the heel.
When to you is declared the beginning of water in the heel by the signs which I have said in the division, then begin and give to drink to the patient water that purifies the head of him, and guard that from all humidities.
And do that suzar in bath in degu for some days.
And then command him to shave his head, and cauterize that with a cautery in the middle location of the head; and then cauterize that with two cauteries over two temples if it is the beginning of the descent of water in two heels, or of one side if it is the beginning of the water in one heel.
Incise with cautery all the veins and arteries which are left the coden; and be the cauteries in that length in the latitude of the temples.
And guard yourself from fluxes of blood when it is cauterized; and if you see of him fluxes of blood, stop him with some medicine, the one which is to you possible.
And you will come with wisdom the one which is in the extraction of arteries and with the abscess of those and caution of fluxes of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the neck below two bones with two cauteries deliberately produced.
Chapter XIII.
Of cauterization of ancient tears.
When tears of the heels are ancient and by the veins and arteries which are in the manifest location of the head outside and it is verified that this is superfluity frigid phlegmatic, then cauterize that with the cautery which we have recounted in the chapter of the beginning of water descending in the heels, and with a cautery in the middle location of the head and with two cauteries in the neck below two temples, and with two cauteries in the neck below two bones. And if you need of addition, then cauterize that in all width of the heel's tail over the extremity of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Chapter XIV.
Of cauterization of stench of the nose.
When you medicate that with the water which we have said in the division and it does not profit your medication, then you equip and give to drink to the patient the cochias for three nights; and then shave the head of him, and cauterize him with a middle cautery with olive cautery. And then cauterize that with a pointed cautery with two cauteries above the two eyebrows, leaving the hair a little.
And guard yourself from the arc that you do not burn that.
And of the pointed cautery this is the form.
Chapter XV.
Of cautery for softening eyelids of the wheels.
When the eyelid of the wheel is softened by illness or by humidity, then cauterize that eyelid with a cautery with this lunar cautery; and this is the form of it:
And if you, cauterize that above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries in all part, and be elongated from the temples. And be the length of each cautery according to the quantity of the eyebrow.
And do not press too much your hand with the cautery, but according to the quantity that the third part of the eyelid be cauterized.
Chapter XVI.
Of cautery of the eyelid of the wheel when the hairs are converted to the parts of them and pierce the wheel.
When the hairs of the wheel are converted to the parts of them so that they pierce the wheel, cauterize in those in two manners, because cauterize or is with fire or is with medicine comburent.
If with cautery of it with fire, command the patient in front of it that he see his hairs as those which they are washed, until they are prolonged and equalized; and if you pierce that of them, then you strengthen the wheels of it with a bandage so that it is not bad until the hairs are born.
Therefore, as they are born and equalized, then place the head of the patient in your see, and then send over the eyelid of the wheels of it with a tent, with a sign which is according to the figure of a leaf of myrtle, and be the beginning of the sign near the hairs.
And then place a poultice embedded in a white of egg or in a mucilage of ptilli on the wheel.
And then ignite the cautery of which this is the form of it.
And then cauterize over the figure which you have signed, little by little, in several times, until the surface of the codena which is as a myrtle leaf, be entirely burned properly.
And sign of health of your work is that you see the eyelid of the wheel already be contracted and the hairs of it be elevated above the puncture of the wheel.
And therefore elevate your hand and leave it for three days, and then place over it a poultice with border until the scabra be eradicated. And then cure it with an enguent until it be healed.
But if it returns for the hairs any cause to their puncture and the eyelid is softened, then do another time the cautery over that all as you had done first.
But if the hairs are in the eyelid of it, then cauterize that until it be elevated to its natural place and be equalized and that the hairs do not pierce the wheel.
But the cautery with medicine comburent this is that you command the patient that he see the hairs until they are prolonged and equalized, and then be made of a cloth the form of a myrtle leaf.
And then take of known soap and of live cause a un. i., i., or that, and then mix those causes well, and make it with a festinacio so that it not be frozen; and then expand it of it over the cloth which is made as the form of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the one wheel or with both; and place over the wheel a poultice embedded in a white of egg, and the head of the patient be in your see.
And place the said over the medicine and press it a little and no the mauguas until the patient feels the bite of the medicine, because bite is in it as of fire.
And therefore as he will perceive that the other bite, then leave the medicine and make it with your said; therefore as ceases the bite, then remove the medicine and wash the wheel with water; and then consider if times the eyelid is already lifted as it is washed above the constriction with fire or with incision, because then it is well; and if it returns over that of the medicine on the place in which it has not put the medicine and does not degrade until it be equalized your operation and be contracted the wheel.
And then place over it a poultice with border until the scabra of the adhesion be eradicated, and then cure it with an enguent deafinicon or with another until it be healed.
And it is necessary to you, above your operation that you guard with pervigil diligence that in the wheel does not fall re of the medicine, and if the eyelid apropos some days is softened and some cause of the hairs pierce in the wheel, then iterate your medicine over that place the which of the eyelid is softened, and properly as you have done at the beginning, and then enaviro it until it be healed.
And this is the form of a myrtle leaf.
And know that the wheels of men are diversified according to the magnitude and the smallness, and therefore according to that is made your constriction.
And no one will be concealed the way of rightness to him who is studying in this art.
Chapter XVII.
Of cauterization of fistula that is in the lacrimal of the heel.
When you cure a fistula with what we have said in the divisions of the illnesses and do not confer your cure, then you must cauterize it according to this manner: command the patient to put his head in your lap, and hold the head of him some minister between your hands in such a manner that it is not troubled nor agitated with his head.
And then place a cloth soaked in oil or in a poultice of ptilli on the heel of him.
And then ignite the cautery of which this is the form:
Which is concave, as is the form of a reed or a vulture's feather, from one extremity of which the cautery is made.
And if you wish, it be penetrating into the other extremity. And if you wish, let it be sorted as it tends.
But however, that which is concave is better for your work.
And then press the fistula if it is open, and draw out of it blood and dry that. And if it is not open, then open it and extract the pus from it.
And then place on it the cautery which is well ignited, and keep with that your hand a little distance from the cautery of the heel to the part of the nose, so that it does not burn your hand or the patient be troubled, and then place the cautery on the grains of the heel and corrupt that.
And therefore if at the beginning of your cauterization it penetrates into the bone, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, if it is necessary; and leave it so for three days, and then place on it a cloth with border and surround it with an exsiccating enguent until it is healed.
But if after eleven days it is not healed, then place on it a medicine sharp and corrosive until the bone is uncovered and it is scraped according to what you have ordained in your chapter.
And there is another manner of cauterizing a fistula which some first said:  Insert into the place of the fistula and make a hole there and then place in that fissure a fine cautery of which this is the form: And pour into that the quantity of one ounce of melted lead; and keep your hand with the cautery with good retention, and do not trouble the patient so that the melted lead does not reach the heel of him; and when you place on the heel of the patient a cloth soaked in oil or in water, because lead adheres to the place of the fistula and heals it by a marvelous healing.
And if the fistula is healed with what we have said of the cauterization and the cure, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to administer trauc from the nose and reduce the fistula to the core of the nose according to what will come in its proper place.
Chapter XVIII.
Of cauterization of the fissure of the potz.
Many times fissures occur in the lips, and mostly in the lips of children.
Therefore, as you cure those fissures with what we have said in the divisions and it does not profit your cure, then ignite the small cautery knife according to this form which is:
And let its concavity be according to the fineness of a cottle.
Then place that init carefully in those fissures until the cautery reaches the bottom of the fissures.
And then cure that with cerotz until it is healed.
Chapter XIX.
Of cauterization of a fistula in the mouth.
When in the root of the uvula or in the palate or in the roots of the teeth there happens an abscess and then it breaks, and then it is old, and pus flows and a fistula is made, and then you cure that and your cure does not profit, then you must ignite a cautery according to the quantity that is received in the fistula, and then place that ignited in the tract of the fistula, and keep your hand so that it reaches the iron ignited to the bottom of it, and at the back of it do so once or twice; and then cure that with the water that we have said of the cure until it is healed.
And therefore if the pus is abscised and is healed, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to discover the place and host the corrupted bone according to what will come in its chapter.
Chapter XX.
Of cauterization of the teeth and of softening of the angivas.
When the angivas are softened by humidity and the teeth are bad, and you cure those with medicines and it does not profit, then place the head of the patient in your lap, and then ignite the cautery the form of which will come close so that you place the point on the tooth and introduce into that the ignited cautery quickly, and keep your hand a little so that the patient feels the heat of the fire at the root of the tooth being reached.
And then take your hand, and then repeat the cautery several times according to what you wish.
And then the patient gargles with salt water and keeps it for an hour, then spits it out, because the bad tooth is stopped, the gums are softened and the corrupted humidity is dried.
Chapter XXI.
Of cauterization of tooth pain.
When tooth pain is due to coldness, or there is a worm in it, or it does not respond to treatment with medicine, then cauterization is done in that tooth in two ways: cauterization with a cow's horn or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with horn is that you take the horn of a cow and heat it in a blacksmith's forge, and then take a handle and wrap it around the tip of the horn, and then immerse that in the heated horn, and place it on the painful tooth, pressing it firmly until it is seared.
And then repeat this several times until the force of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool or cloth in the heated horn, and place it on the painful tooth, and place a red-hot iron on top of it until the iron reaches the edge of the cavity of the tooth.
But however, cauterization with fire is that you attend to the handle of the iron or the metal, and it has some thickness in it, and the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then ignite the cauterizer, the shape of which will come, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand over it until the cauterizer is seared; and do this several times because the pain is reduced either on that day or the next day.
And cover that, by the application of that cauterizer, the patient gargles with warm water and keeps it for an hour, and then spits it out; and this is the shape of the cauterizer.
And cauterize with whichever extremity you wish, according to what is possible for you.
And this is the shape of the cannula:
Chapter XXII.
Of cauterization of extrophulos.
When extrophulos are of phlegm and humors that are cold and do not respond to digestion by medicines and you wish to digest them slightly, then you ignite the cauterizer whose shape is this following, having two thick extremities so that the smoke of the cauterizer can escape through the other extremity, and place it on that abscess once, and another if you deem it necessary, until it reaches the edge of the abscess.
And if the abscess is small, then place the cauterizer according to the size of the abscess, and then leave it for three days and place a cloth soaked in warm water on top of it until the water that the fire has combusted is reduced.
And then treat this with gargles and compresses and bandages until it is healed.
Chapter XXIII.
Of cauterization of sore throat and constriction of the throat.
When the humors come upon the throat, and most when this is of cold constitution, then it is necessary that the patient be evacuated at the beginning with laxative medicines, and then cauterize that of the root of the larynx in the depressed area.
And be careful that you do not reach the cauterizer to the larynx nor burn the soft tissue of it except a little.
And cauterize that with another cauterizer at the junction of the neck in the lower vertebra of it. And the cauterizer of it be a pointed one according to the previous manner.
And then treat this with the water that is preceded until it is healed.
Chapter XXIV.
Of cauterization of lung disease and cough.
When cough and lung disease are of cold humors and the patient has no fever or phlegm and it is an old illness, then cauterize that with two cauterizers on the breastbone in the depressed areas of the ribs and sternum; and with another cauterizer in the middle of the foot between the two toes; and be the cauterizer pointed according to the previous form.
And if you wish, be your cauterization pointed with the cauterizer that is called a point, the shape of which you have seen in the cauterization of ear pain.
And make points within those; and then treat this with the water that is preceded until it is healed.
And may the cauterizer have three ramps so that cauterization is done in this way: at one time you can make three cauterizations according to this form:
Chapter XXV.
Of cauterization of the tithing that is the head of the helper.
When the head of the helper is dislocated due to lubricating humors and it is not fixed at the time of its return to its place, then it is necessary to reduce the dislocation before it returns to its place, and through a small movement it is dislocated as it should, as we have testified, then first reduce the dislocation, and the patient is placed on his back or on his side; and then elevate the tissue that is in the front part of the cheek to the lower parts with the fingers of your left hand, if the joint is dislocated on the front part.
And then light the cautery having two heads; and this is its shape:
And then cauterize the chain while it penetrates one into the other; and the figure of cauterization will then be of four cauteries.
And sometimes it is adjusted according to this count and because they are the cauteries viii.
And then place on the cautery porys cuytz with salt, and then make the patient adhere to tranquility, and the limb not be harmed for any time until it is comforted.
And if the dislocation is at the parts above and tart is done, then cauterize over the muscle with a cautery clavilh or with motz cauteris puntan, for the joint is confirmed and the humidity is removed and the patient is healed.
Chapter XXVI.
Of cauterization of the stomach.
When there comes in the stomach fire and many humidities that that extract from its complexion and so multiply raumas in it, and if you continue the ways of cure and do not confer it, then it comes that the patient is upon his two supinations, and extends his arms and his thighs, and then cauterize that with three cauteries: one cautery left the foot for the quantity of a finger with cautery clavilh, and with two cauteries left of the two sides of the cautery, until the figure of cautery triangular; and elongate between those that are not adjusted that they will make poyredura.

Of cauterization of the liver fire.
When there comes in the liver pain for fire, or for humidity, or for gross windiness, until its normal complexion is cast by superfluous egress, and it is cured the patient with that which we have said and do not confer it, then it comes that the patient is supinated upon his neck, and senhes with tent three cauteries according to this form and this quantity metess over the liver left of the ipocondres, the hon perve the decubit of man.

Chapter XXVIII.
Of perforation of abscess of the liver with cautery.
When there comes an incision or abscess in the liver and you want to know if that abscess is in the flesh of the liver or in its tunic, then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the patient atrobo gravitates and pain ses acuitat.
And if it is in the tunic of the liver, with the pain is acuitat great and times that already afatiguatz the doctors the cure of him.
Therefore, cove that the patient is reversed upon his neck; and then senhes the location of the abscess with tent; and then light the cautery the which is assembled to rag, the form of which a precedit in the other page. Chapter XXIX.
Of cauterization of pleurisy.
The ancients said that cauteries of the roots of aristology were used to cauterize according to this manner, and this is the one that you should take from the roots of aristology long and dry a root long and thin that is found, and it should be the thickness of the finger.
And then submerge that in oil and heat that in the fire, and then cauterize with a cautery in that place which is between the continuation of the clavicle and the neck; and with two small cauteries, I have guided, one slightly sloping to the side that is right of the beard, and with two cauteries in that which is sloping between the fifth rib and the shoulder blade, sloping slightly to the sides behind; and another cautery in the middle location of the foot; and another on the stomach, and three cauteries of the sides behind; and one cautery in that place which is between the two shoulder blades, and with two cauteries of the two sides of the foot, besides the cautery which is between the two shoulder blades.
And in the cover that you understand your hand with the cautery, then it should be in the manifest of the code in work.
And already said some ancients that some of the men who use cauteries of iron resembling a ray and ignite that, and put that in that place which is between the ribs, until they reach that abscess and it is forged healthy, thus as we have said in the abscess of the thigh.
But in this perforation with cautery there is no fear, because it dies as soon as it is applied to the location of the fistula to which there is no healing.
Chapter .xxx.
Of the cauterization of the spleen.
When you cure the illness of the spleen with what we have said of the cure in the division and do not confer your cure, then cauterize in it is according to three manners, all of which are straight, of which one is that you make three cauteries or four lines according to the length of the spleen according to the figure of the cauteries of the thigh, the figure of which has preceded.
And be between each cautery the thickness of a finger or a little more, and the manner of the cautery be the manner which we have said in the cautery of the thigh equally.
And do not compress your hand with the cautery; and the patient be placed on his back.
And there is another manner of cauterizing, so it is that you ignite the cautery having two vergences, the cause of which we have said in the chapter of dislocation of the muscle, and elevate the code which is in the straight line of the spleen the horn to reach the lying of the left patient.
And be the elevation with which you elevate the code according to the length of the body, so that cauteries are made according to the latitude of the body.
And then, between the two vergences, ignite the hot, in that entrance where with those you penetrate the code from the other part.
And then, having extracted the cautery; and therefore are made four cauteries.
And if you want, cauterize with a cautery having three vergences.
And then you cure the cautery because it should have been laid aside for too many days, because it is more convenient than the other causes preceding in the cure.
Chapter .xxxI.
Of cauterization of hydrops.
Cauterize not in catz in hydrops but in alcinte3 properly.
When you cure the hydrops with the manners of cure which we have said in the division and do not confer your cure, then cover that you cauterize with four cauteries in the circuit of the navel and with one cautery on the stomach, and another cautery on the thigh, and another cautery on the spleen, and with two cauteries between the vertebrae of the back, and a cautery in the right foot, and another cautery on the stomach. And the quantity of the depth of the cautery be proportionate to the thickness of the code.
And then leave the cautery open so that it gets laid aside for a long time.
And do not evacuate the patient from cure after the cautery with what cover so that two understandings may be added to it, and it is festooned to it with the help of healing.
The form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized is clavilh according to the form of which is used before, and it is the one with which the back is cauterized is olivar according to what is precedent to its form.
Chapter .xxxII.
Of cauterization of feet and of the thighs.
When the feet are abscesses in hydrops and are filled with watery pus, cover that you cauterize the feet on the back of the foot in nocrati, which is between the auricular and the anular, and elevate your hand with the cautery and do not twist that; and then elevate your hand, and do not return that of all, because the watery pus remains.
It is the cautery according to this form: And then make on the two thighs two cauteries, and in each thigh be made cautery with the extremity of the cautery cutellar. And let the cautery be according to the length of the thigh; and let one be placed above and the other below the middle of the thigh; and on each thigh two cauteries.
And leave the wound open for a long time so that no water remains in it.
And then cure it with those causes that have been said.
Chapter .xxxiii.
Of cauterization of the belly.
When the belly is due to cold and humidity that should be within the virtues, so is the digestive and retentive virtue, which are in the stomach and intestines, and it is cured with these ways of curing and not confering, and sometimes the patient suffers cauterization to exhibit virtue, then cauterize it with a large cautery on their stomach according to what has preceded in the cauterization of the stomach, with the cautery of the circle and four cauteries in the circuit of the navel subtle, with a subtle cautery clavilh; and with cautery on the alcatin over alozis great, or with two cauteries.
And if sometimes the humidities are exuberant and the patient tolerates it, then cauterize it on the pentinilh and on the intestines, and firmly adjust two cauteries on the stomach and near the inguinal regions, for it is a perfect cure of benefit from which you will not err.
Chapter .xxxiv.
Of cauterization of old hemorrhoids.
When they are in the nature of old hemorrhoids or one of thick humors cold or of corrupted humidities, and they are cured with what has been said in the division and not confering your cure, then cauterize with three cauteries on the pus below the small of the back and small triangular, and with cautery above the navel cays by two digits.
And if you suspect that the stomach of him be cold and his food not digested, and the face of him sometimes pale, then cauterize it on the stomach with a large cautery according to what has preceded; and with a cautery on the liver, and another cautery on the spleen with a cautery clavilh, and leave the cautery open for some time, and then cure him while he is healing.
Chapter .xxxv.
Of cauterization of a boil near the abscess of it.
When you abscess a boil, then you ignite the cautery that is assembled to a ray. Then introduce that ignited one into that abscess, and end your hand until the cautery reaches the orifice of the vein from which the blood comes.
And do this once or twice, for if the boils are too many, then cauterize each one according to what we have recounted, and then cure those with what you confer to them of the unguents until they are healed.
And if you cauterize with a large cautery on the alcatin, it is more beneficial.
Chapter .xxxvi.
Of cauterization of fistulas that are made in the nature of the lower parts of him.
When nature does not obey the work that we have recounted in its place, and the patient is frightened by it, be healed with cautery.
Therefore, when someone has a fistula in the lower part, and it is old, corroded with pus and corrupted humors, and therefore that which is most worthy is that you probe it with a subtle probe, and then know the quantity of the depth of it with the previously mentioned probe.
Then ignite the cautery that is similar to a ray. And then introduce that ignited cautery into this fistula, and according to the quantity in which the probe enters.
And iterate over that cautery inside until those corrupted parts are burned once or twice or three times, according to the quantity of your need.
And guard yourself from burning of nerves and veins; or if the fistula goes to the bladder or the intestines, then guard yourself from all those places; and do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy place and you think that it is not penetrating.
And then cure the place until it is healed.
And if the place is sealed, and the materials are cut from it, and remain so for a long time, then you know that it is healed entirely.
And if the materials are not from it, then you know that it is penetrating or in the preon of it the corrupted, or comes from those causes of which remembrance will come in its place.
Chapter .xxxvii.
Of cauterization of the boils.
When in the boils it is necessary pain due to cold or thick windiness, and by this the patient's groin is inflamed, then you should cauterize it on the boils with a cautery on each boil with a cautery clavilh of which we previously mentioned the remembrance.
And firmly cauterize them with the second one a little, so that there will be three cauteries lined, and then they will be more beneficial.
Chapter .xxxviii.
Of cauterization of the bladder.
When the bladder is weakened and softened by cold and humidity so that the patient cannot retain urine, then cauterize that area on the part left over the bladder, the side where the hairs of the pubic region begin, and cauterize with one cautery on the right side, and with another on the left side of it.
And the length of each cautery should be according to the quantity of the knots of the pouch; and cauterize that with a cautery in the lowest part of the back, or with two cauteries if it is necessary.
And cauterize with a pointed cautery according to what is processed.
Chapter .xxxix.
Of the cauterization of the thigh.
When cold and humidity come into the thigh, and therefore pregnancy is prohibited, and the menses of her are corrupted, and the provocation of them is delayed, and pain occurs in the place where they come, then it is necessary that the place be cauterized with three cauteries in the circuit of the navel, as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder; and with a cautery on the place left over from the back, or with two cauteries, and be the cautery pointed.
Chapter .xl.
Of the cauterization of the dislocation of the hip.
When moist humors are poured into the part of the hip, and are caused by the inflammation of its place, and a sign of it is that the thigh is prolonged over the other when they are compared between them. And the place of the dislocation is felt in it where it is raised.
Therefore, it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the part of the hip of him with a cautery in a circle shape, as you will have felt with your finger in the circuit of the part as it is turned, and so that the part falls in the middle of the circle.
And be the cautery of which preceded the form in the cauterization of the stomach.
And if this cautery is not present to you, then cauterize that with three cauteries with a large olive cautery.
And be made the cautery according to the quantity of the thickness of the whole bone; and take care of that while it is healing.
Chapter .xli.
Of the cauterization of the sciatic vein.
When pain comes in the part of the hip, and it is caused by cold and humidity, the patient is cured with what we have said and do not confer, and this is ancient, then it is necessary that you lance the patient of thick humors with fetid pills or with artificial pills or similar; and then cauterize that.
And the manner of the cautery in that is according to two manners: the cautery with burning medicines, or the cautery with fire.
It is according to two scientific manners, of which one is that you cauterize that on the part of the hip of him with three triangular cauteries according to this form; and make with those a good depth. And be the spaces the which is between each cautery the quantity of the thickness of the finger and if the olive cautery or large.
Sometimes, however, the cautery is on the middle part over the head of the hip so that there are four cauteries.
And if you want, cauterize with the circle of which is preceded the form in the cauterization of the dislocation of the hip, that is, a circle containing and burning the thickness of the whole bone.
And this is the manner of cauterizing the sciatica when pain is adherent to the hip and does not extend into the thigh.
But if it extends into the thigh, then cauterize that with two cauteries on the thigh on the place where you feel the pain of the patient; and with one cautery on the hip for four fingers a little below the fleshy part.
And if the cautery is a knife, and be the depth of the cautery according to the quantity of the thickness of the bone.
And if the patient feels that the pain extends into the place near the toes, then cauterize that here where you feel it with a cautery for three points or four or more if it is necessary of that.
And if the patient feels pain below the hip and towards the thigh, then cauterize that here with a knife cautery.
And guard yourself in all cauterization that you do not end with the cautery as much as you burn nerves or large arteries, and that by that to you is over the patient no harm or contraction.
And you have already seen one or another of those who cauterized on the hip and ended in the cauterization, and the leg burned inflated until the tumor reached the foot, and burning and corrupted the whole foot. And then a strong acid solution of the belly, and by that death.
And if the pain is in two parts at once, cauterize each one according to this manner.
And the wise ones said in the cauterization of the hip, a cautery of which this is the manner: make a circle of iron whose circuit is the majority of a palm; and be its orifice according to the thickness of a finger bone or a little less.
And within that circle make another third; and let the space which is between them be the quantity of the night of the foot; and let those circles be open on two sides; and let the length of those cages be a night or two nights, and make in those margins of iron decently adorned in the circles; and this is the form of it:
Then let it be ignited in the fire until it becomes red and throws sparks, and then let it be placed on the part of the ankle, the patient lying on their side. And therefore cauterize that with three red-hot cauteries at once.
And then leave that for three days; then plaster that with butter and leave the wound open for too many days; and then cure that with ointments until it is healed.
Says Albucasis: O, sons, of this kind of cautery we have used little because of the terror of its appearance, and for that reason we have found few who guard over it.
May the cauteries to those who suffer them, and those who are treated with it, be few.
But cauteries with medicinal ointments are that you make two circles having a perforated arm in which they should place the handle of the iron gate; let the length of the sides in the breadth of them be two nights or as many as those.
And if the space which is between them be the quantity of the thickness of the finger; and let them be open below and above, and let them contain themselves between them according to this form:
And then place your hand over the part of the ankle; the patient lying on their side, and compress your hand over the part of the ankle; and then take of warm water and pour it between the two circles, and the quality of that be with the small fire little by little, and keep that for the quantity of an hour, and suffer the patient the biting and burning of it — for that biting is so as of fire — until the biting ceases.
And then raise your hand with the instrument and wipe away the warm water from all the ankle with cool water.
And then leave that for three days and place upon that butter until the blackness of the burning is removed, and leave that for some days, and it will run from it pus; this is the end in healing.
And then cure that with ointments until it is healed.
And if the pain is extended into the thigh or the leg, make to it a statue in it which contains water as it is made in the ankle equally.
And this is the manner of warm water, and you have already written that in the treatise of the rectification of medicines. Take of alkali and of caustic, of each one part, and mix them and place them in a new vessel of which the lower part is perforated by a small hole, according to the quantity that enters into it.
And place below the bottom of the vessel another vessel inverted, and pour upon that alkali and caustic warm water which covers them for a finger, and as soon as you compress them with your hand for good compression, and leave the vessel that descends from it water sharp in the lower part of the inverted vessel.
And then adjust all that water, and pour it over other caustic and other renewed alkali, for that the hour is of strong sharpness, which is administered in many operations of medicine and in cauterization of the other members, for operation does of fire.
And so of the medicines some with which is cauterized much, as tezzizic and honey anacrat and caustic with sabao in such a way that they are mixed.
And Gualia recounts of an ancient man the operation and cure with which is cured pain of ankle and of sciatic vein, and magnifies much being of that, and says that there is no need of other cure, and that it is healed for one time as it recounts, for strong he that intertwine in bath and already sees of that.
And it is that it be taken of green fig, and if it is not found green, be taken recent fig; and much be minced with a little of grease and be placed upon the ankle in which is the pain, or in the thigh, or in the leg, and be bound.
And be left for the quantity of three hours or for the quantity that the patient feels cessation of the burning.
And then put that in bath and once the body of it be red, put that in the sun, for the pain ceases and it is healed.
And know that no one should use cauteries with these medicines except for the evacuation of the body.
But already Escorides says that when with the wound of goat the sciatic vein is cauterized, it profits him very well; and let the cautery be with it according to this manner: take wool and be it dipped in old oil, and be placed between the toes of the foot and between the bones.
And then take dry goat's wound and inflame that with fire until it be made charcoal; and place it upon the wool and leave it until it be extended. And then iterate that, and do not cease to do that until the feeling of the biting reaches into the ankle and repauses the pain.
And this manner of cautery is called cautery of goats.

Chapter .xliii.
Of cauterization at the beginning of jaundice.
Often this illness befalls young children; and a sign of its beginning in children is that they accidentially stumble upon their structure in the ale and raise and move it.
And it appears in the last vertebra of the back and of its nodes that already begins to rise above the other vertebrae.
And therefore when you see this and want to prohibit it, then cauterize that with a cautery that is circular according to this form: that presses the cautery over all parts of the vertebra evenly.
And if you wish, cauterize in the circuit of the vertebra with the pointed cautery two or three lines. And let the points be close together.
And after cure the place until it is healed with what we have said.
But beware that cauterization is not administered in jaundice that is made by spasm of a nerve.
Chapter .xliv.
Of cauterization of gout and joint pain.
When joint pain is caused by cold humors that infiltrate each part of the body, and pain occurs in the feet, it is customarily called gout by doctors.
And therefore as gout caused by cold is cured by method of cure and not only the pains are removed, then the pains are removed by cauterization.
And it is that you cauterize that after evacuation in the circuit of the joint of the foot with many cauteries.
And let it be an olive cautery of which this is the form of it:
And if it is necessary to make points on the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery. And if the pains rise into the tendons or to the other joints, and this many times happens, then cauterize that on each tendon with three or four cauteries of all parts with this olive cautery.
And if many cauteries that these cauteries are necessary to you, then cauterize that and do not press too much your hand with the cautery before, be only around the form of the bone.
And if the pains rise into the tendon of the back, then administer the cautery which we have said in its chapter.
And if the pains are in the muscles only, and it is called suagra, then prick in the circuit of the fossae as they turn, prick in those two lines.
And if the pains remain in the fingers, then prick in the circuit of the fossae on each node and on the knuckle of the hand.
And if the pains rise to certain joints in the elbows or to the muscles, then cauterize those of all parts of the joints.
And do not evacuate the patient of good regimen and reception of medicines, because if it is done good regimen and the flacma is evacuated with this cautery it is healed, God help.
Chapter .xlv.
Of cauterization of ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin and the intestines appear before the hernia, and this begins to approach, then you command the patient to leave their food in their day and use of lenitive causes so that the wound descends from their belly.
And after follow the patient between your hands on his back, and command him to keep his leg until it is thrown or the hernia or the intestines appear.
And after return that with your fingers and feel with ten the rupture on the bone of the pelvis with a sign the extremity of which is similar to the majority of a circle on the upper parts of the body.
And after ignite the cautery of which this is the form of it:
until it is very hot and throws sparks. And then return the intestine or hernia to its cavity, and place your hand over the area so that the intestine does not come out.
And you have already opened the space between the patient's thighs, placed a cushion under them, another servant on their legs, and another on their chest, holding their hands.
And then place the cautery over that sign with your hand holding the cautery straight, and you must insert that into the space between the bones of the penile shaft into the middle of the urethra; and repeat with that other time if you haven't succeeded in the first attempt to insert the bone.
And observe carefully the movement of the intestine during the cauterization, so that you do not burn the intestine so that on the patient there does not come death or other great harm.
And know that when you with the cautery do not touch the bones, do not consider your operation.
And know that the cautery of children should be subtle according to their size and measure.
And then care for the location of the cautery for three days with a border until the scar of the fire is healed.
And then care for that with the other ointments until it is healed.
And the patient shall lie on their back for forty days until the location and the plague are sealed.
And know that you should pause the nourishment of him according to the length of time of his healing, which lines his belly, and that the intestine does not come out from the effort of healing.
And then when he wants to get up after forty days, then administer a decent amount of food, and keep that for another forty days.
And be moderate in work and repletion of food and drink, and of voice vehemently, for when he uses this regimen of healing entirely he will be healed.
And you say the healing of ruptures in other parts of the belly, and so at the beginning, and you want them not to pull, then cauterize the rupture of that with a round cautery according to the quantity of it, and it should be that which is exhumed from the chain as if the third part of it; and then care for that with what we have said, and it is not adjusted.
And already some first ones say that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery according to this form, because it is marked with a tent:
And it is placed a line that goes by the latitude in the part most superior of the rupture, and another line below; and place your hand with a pointed cautery, but the first cautery is lighter and better.
Chapter .xlvi.
Of cauterization of torsion.
When in some members by accident or by percussion pain and that pain persists for a long time and does not confer to the cure with medicines, then know that you should cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And be the cautery of every member according to its magnitude and its smallness, and its virtue and weakness, and location of torsion and pain of it.
Therefore, if it is healed by the first cautery, well is; and if not, then repeat on it the cautery; for by custom of those pains is that they are pointed members to that member which approaches to it, so that know that you should cauterize those until the patient is healed.
Chapter .xlvii.
Of cauterization of leprosy.
Leprosy some times with cautery for great benefit, and more so if the species of leprosy that is made by putrefaction of flame and melancholy.
And therefore, as you want to cauterize that, consider if the leprosy is common and has that cured with what we have said in the division and do not say, nor is it, and fear that the corruption comprehends the whole body of it and the whole complexion of it, then cauterize that on the head with 5 cauteries: one in the middle place of the head, and the second farther from it, and the front to the end of the hairs; and two on two horns; and one behind, on the nape or service.
And finish your hand with the cautery a little while until it impresses on the bone a small impression, and from it the scabs are displaced, so that the expiration of gross vapors is relieved from it; and cauterize on the flesh according to what is necessary.
And if the leprosy is already expanded over the patient and appears manifestly, then know that you should cauterize that with those cauteries which we have said in the head; and with a cautery on the extremity of the nose, and with two cauteries on the two cheekbones, and with two cauteries on two vertebrae of the neck, and with six cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and one large one on the vertebrae near the hip, and one on the rib, and with two on the ankles, and one on each ankle, and with two on the knees, and one on each knee, and with two on the elbows, and with two on the muscles, and with two on the tendons of their feet; and cauterize that on all the joints of the fingers of the hands and feet, and on each heel of their feet, and on the hollows of their hands.
And guard yourself from the nerves which are on the heel that you do not burn those.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery on the bone of the penis and with another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that as much as you adjust cauteries, so much is more beneficial and more conferring; and know that the patient does not have in the cautery pain, as if they have their own, for so the body of it is already stupefied.
And the size of the cauteries should be great or few according to the limbs and joints according to what was said before about the kinds of instruments.
And then cure the cauteries with flour of herbs mixed with honey and the other cure within which it is healed.
Chapter XLVIII.
Of the cauterization of stupor.
When some limb is numbed or asleep and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not healed, then you cauterize that numbed limb with cauteries according to what merits the size of the limb or its smallness.
And let your cautery enter the thickness of the bone a little. And then cure that with an ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes cauterization is done on some stupor which originates in the hips and feet, and in the vertebrae of the lower back and where the nerves emerge that move that limb, and the stupor is removed.
But do not presume about this more than he who is wise in the anatomy of the limbs and the egress of the nerves of the whole body moving.
Chapter XLIX.
Of the cauterization of ulcers that are mortified.
When an ulcer is old and does not respond to any of the medicinal ointments, then you cauterize over that with a cautery, preon a little, according to the quantity of the thickness of the bone, until it is removed the whiteness and the color of it, and the color of it is changed.
And then cure that with flour of herbs and lentils mixed with rose oil and leaves of arnica, and blood of dove or blood of round, from each one a part and all are mixed, and then let a linen cloth be laid and placed on the location until it is healed.
Chapter L.
Of the cauterization of a boil.
When a boil begins and you want to stop it, then cauterize that with a circular cautery around its circuit, as it is revolved.
And the wise say that it should be cauterized with the back cautery in the middle location; but to me, this is not seen, because I fear that it will be ulcerated, and I have already seen this some times.
And it is more straightforward that it be cauterized in its circuit with a circle, as we have said, or with pointed cauteries.
Chapter LI.
Of the cauterization of abscesses.
When some abscess is delayed in maturation, and thus it is because of the superfluity that makes it, or because of the patient's age, because he is old or decrepit, of little blood, or because of time, and you want to hasten the maturation of the abscess; then cauterize in its circuit with small pointed cauteries; and then let that be, because it will have hastened in maturation.
But if you want the perforation of it with a cautery, then you ignite the cautery of which this is the form of it: and place that in the middle location of the abscess until it penetrates the bone.
And if the cautery in that location that is farthest, so that the body of the arm be relieved; and then cure that until it is healed.
Chapter LII.
Of the cauterization of a rodent.
A rodent is a corruption that walks in the limb, which corrodes that as if a fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you see that rodent in a location that suffers cauterization with fire, then you ignite cauteries, small and pointed, a few, and large according to what is convenient in that location where the rodent is.
And then cauterize that from all parts until you eradicate all the corruption and no cause of it remains.
And then leave that for three days, and place over the cauterized locations a cloth soaked in oil mixed until all the scars are eradicated and all the corruption.
And then cure that with ointments that generate flesh.
But if after three days you see that the flesh grows healthy in which there is no corruption, well; but if not, then repeat the cautery over that which is raw in the corrupted locations.
And a rodent is medicated some times with sharp medicine, because that is placed in the location of cautery. But however, cauterization with fire is of more lighter help.
And I have already said the cure of it with sharp medicine in the division, and therefore take that when from it you will have need.
Chapter LIII.
Of the cauterization of claws and of other similar things.
Many times there is a malady that is called a claw in the lower parts of the foot, and it is a large, deep cause, which bends the foot; and cauterization in those is done in two ways, so it is cauterization with fire and cauterization with boiling water.
But cauterization with fire is that you ignite the cautery concave, similar to the beak of a vulture, which be made of iron according to the quantity which contains the claw from all parts, and be of subtle margins.
And then place that lit [object] on the key, and then turn your hand with the cautery around the key until the cautery reaches the depth of the key. And leave it for three days until it begins to sweat. And then plaster it with wild herbs crushed with salt, and leave the plaster on it for one night, so that it is eradicated from its roots.
And then cure the area with a rinse of generative flesh until it is healed.
And if it is not converted, and many times it happens on the surface of the body, mostly in the arms and feet, then you must administer cauterization in those with water, and that you take a tube of lead or iron or a vulture's feather, and place it on the key; and then put in the tube a small quantity of water, and hold your hand, and you turn it with compression of your hand of all, and press the edge of the tube in the root of the key, and it will absorb the small amount of water through the vein of the root of the key; and wait for the patient a little bit the bite of the small amount of water for an hour, and then remove it, because the key with its roots is eradicated.
And thus do it to those and the other until you come over all of them in the body.
And then cure those pus that the roots of the keys are eradicated with this of the rinses that the flesh generates.
Chapter .liiii.

When someone has a tremor due to fire in the nerve or fever of a burning cause, or by another similar cause, then you must cauterize it with four cauteries or five on the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra with a cautery; and with cautery on the feet of him, and on his stomach, with olive cautery.
And the tremor of him is rested and hastened the health of the burning illness.

When in the body there are white spots, and they are pustules split that are made of coarse corrupted matters; therefore, at the beginning when it appears, it must be cauterized over all the head of the fistula with a subtle cautery with myrtle twigs, the extremity of which is extended with fire; or with roots of long erestologia; or with a lenticular cautery.
