Chapter lvi.
Of cauterization of blood flow accident by incision of artery.
Many times there is a blood flow from an artery that is incised, the wound which must be closed, or the incision of abscesses or cauterization of the limb, and then similar, and it is difficult to remove that.
Therefore, when it happens to someone, then you must cover with your hand the orifice of the artery, and place on it your finger, pressing it tightly many times until the flow of blood stops from your finger, and that it does not come out.
And then place in the fire the few and large olive cauteries, by number many, and exhale over them while they are burning.
And then take from those one small or one large according to the place and the wound in which the artery is broken, on that vein, quickly, pus that you have removed your finger, and place the cautery until it is cauterized and restricted that blood.
And if the blood is expelled from the orifice of the artery when you remove your finger and extract the cautery, then take another cautery carefully from the cauteries that in the fire are prepared, and therefore do not cease to do this one after another until the blood is restricted.
And guard yourself that you do not burn the nerve that is here, and that it comes upon the patient another evil.
And know that when from the artery blood flows, then it is not possible in those to restrict the blood, and especially when the artery is large, if not by one of four ways: or by cautery as we have said, or by extraction when it is not extracted, because when it is extracted the extremities of him are well burned and the blood is restricted, or that it is tied with a thread or with a ligament for strong structure, or that medicines are placed on it whose virtue is to restrict the blood; and they are tightened with a cushion with decent constriction.
But he who administers decent restriction of him with a ligament and with structure with cloths or by position of burning causes and similar things, do not confer otherwise than briefly.
But if this happens to someone and the physician is not present nor medicine, then open with the placement of the finger indicated on the orifice of that vein as we have said, and understand the great constriction of it until the blood is stopped from the sovereign part of the wound, and on the artery the finger is not removed; and over the artery be sprinkled with cold water of great frigidity until the blood is coagulated and thickened; and more sew in that which must be cauterized or of medicine necessity.

First Chapter.
Of the cure of the water which is contained in the head of children.
Know that this illness often happens to children during childbirth and when the midwife tightens the head of the child, its vitality is affected.
And sometimes it happens for a hidden cause which is not known.

Second Chapter.
When a catarrh or wound occurs in the foot or leg, and it does not get better with treatment, and the medicine does not help, then the last resort is the incision of those two arteries.
And therefore, when you want to incise those arteries, the patient raises their head, and you press the area with a rough cloth so that the arteries are apparent, and you tightly bind the patient's neck with some cloth; and you consider where the vein is; and the places of each one are above the places which are near the ears, and they are hidden unless in some men.
And then you press on the artery with your finger, and you cut each one with a sharp pointed spatula, making the incision reach into the bone, and this is done by the width of the head.
And if you wish, you put the spatula inside the artery and break it at the incisions at the upper parts.
And the length of the incision is about two fingers' width, because when any vein is incised, the blood is emitted with pulsatile egress, which jumps out by frequent jumps.
But if the artery does not appear to the touch, then you measure from the ear the quantity of space of three fingers, and then you press with your finger, and make the incision into the bone.
And this is the quantity of blood that you should get rid of is the quantity of one ounce. And do not get more or less than this, and all this is according to the quantity which appears of the virtue of the patient and the repletion of the artery of him.
And then consider the plaque, and therefore if there remains on the bone any cause of the cicatrix, then incise it so that it does not become a cautery abscess.
And then strengthen the plaque with cotton and bandages of cloth, and care for it with ointments until it heals.
Chapter .iii.

And that which is lighter in the extraction of artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cautery having two handles, because you have marked the two places with a probe, and pause a little, not igniting, until they reach the bone and dissect the vein in two places, so that it is elongated that which is between the extremities of it, because they are not consolidated altogether with this cautery.

And this work is better in all works and lighter.

Chapter V.
Of the cure of ulcers by catartz and on the heels descending from the parts dintz of the head.

Chapter VI.
Of the cure of that which catz in the ears.
Every cause that catz in the ears is one of four species, whether it is mineral stone or a similar cause like iron and lead, or it is of a plant like thistle or bean, or it is a fluid cause like wine and vinegar and their likes, or some beast.
And therefore when stone catz in the ear or another cause similar to those causes that do not fit or grow in the ear, and place the ear in the sunlight, and if you see the stone, then distill into it some cause of violet oil or sesame, and then administer the extract of it, and make the patient snort with a condition, and plug the nostrils to prevent the event of snorting. And then place in the circuit of the ear some pieces of cloth or wool, and extend the ear to the parts above, for many times it is forced-driven with these causes.
And if it is not driven out, then administer the extract of it with the instrument called the gesti epicicarios subtil of which this is the form:
And if it is driven out with the gesti, well is it; and if not, then administer the extract of it with a subtle onci of little duplication.

Of the cure of alconati.
This illness which is called alconati is nothing but a swelling which is adjusted in the wool resembling descending water and is not that.
But the manner of working in it is that you make the patient lie on the saddle arranged and straight, and then take his head in your two hands and move it so that you see the swelling come to the lower parts, and then let it dry and not descend, and keep the light, and the patient sees the causes as he sees.
And if it does not descend below, you know that it is water.
But if the descent is not prepared to the swelling with the water that we have said, then make the patient lie between your hands and then take a fine spatula and finish on that over the panniculus, separating a little of the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea in the crown (in the place where it is void), until the swelling is discharged.
Therefore, when it is discharged, then you distill into the wool water cauda in which you have mixed honey or water in which you have already boiled fennel and honey.
And then cure it with the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter XXII.
Of the cure of the descending water of the wool.
We have already said the species of the water in the division and which convenes to pierce with a sermo declaring, then that according to the health.
Now, therefore, you must make the patient lie between your hands on a cushion and tie his wool tightly.
And then place your left hand near the eyelid of his wool if the wool in which is the water is the left one; or on your right hand, if the wool is the right one.
And then with your right hand take the almond, if the wool is left; or with your left hand, if the wool is right.
And then place the tip of the almond near the crown for the thickness of the ray in the album of the wool from the part of the lower lacrimal, and then press the almond with virtue and revolve your hand on that.
And then penetrate into the album of the wool and feel that the almond has already arrived at the void cause.
And then, let the measure of the path of the almond to the edge be the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness, and it is the crown of the wool; for you will see with that pupil the vision of the wool by the clarity of the tunic cornea.
And then place the almond into the place where is the water, and then you throw it down once, then another, and then if the water descends quickly, then immediately wet the patient's wool with water, and the almond in his wool.
And then rest for a while; then if the water has descended, then you remove that other time before the almond is thrown.
And then when it is dried and does not descend, then you extract the almond with ease, and revolve it with your hand little by little, and then dissolve in the water a little of clear salt of gemma and with that wash the wool from within; and then place outside the wool a cotton or a wool infused in rose oil and egg album and lick the wool with water.
But not those who are of our time, place on that with commi trissat with egg album.
And if you do not obey your almond to the entrance of the wool because of its hardness — for it is some of the men whose wool is hard a lot — then you must take the spatula which is called alberid of which this is the form:
And then pierce with that that conjunction, and do not end your hand in the trace, and it is not if you do not make a path for the almond location subtle.
And then introduce the almond as we have said.
And you must complete the work, be prepared for the patient to sleep comfortably in a bed made in a dark room, and be prohibited from all movements.
And pause in his nature so that his nature may be cleansed, and do not turn his head to the right or left at all.
And be the bandage according to his disposition within the third day.
And then unwrap that in that dark room and prohibit the sight of the wound, and make him see some causes, and then return the bandage within the seventh day.
And do not cover that which you have done at the hour of the cures or as soon as the infusion. You must cover that so that the water may lightly pass through with great and vehement regard.
But if an abscess occurs, then you must unwrap the wound before the seventh day, and rectify that with water that yields pus.
Then you shall cover the sight of him and pause over his face oral so that his movement be regulated, leaving him for some days, him existing in the dark room.
And then be taken from that room gradually and converse in his causes.
And know that in alchemy the disciple is not excused from vision some times, and then you shall be bold about the operation.
And already has it come to us from some of those who are at Artach, and some said that he made fire in the Ayrac magdaam perforated with the which water is sucked.
But however, I have not seen in our land anyone who had perfected water, nor have I read about it in some of the books of the ancients; and it is possible that this is novel.
And these are the forms of the species of magdaan so that it may be over those who ignore those:
And they are made of iron or of iron properly, and their extremities are with this triangular subtlety, the acute extremity thus as it is the form.
Chapter XXIV.
Of the cure of flesh wounds in the nose.
When in the nose are born diverse flesh growths from which some cause is assembled like a scorpion of moth's weight, or a polyp weighty; and this malady is called polyp because it is in resemblance of that weight represented. And of this is cancerous flesh, a lapping, of a dusky color; and of this is that flesh leon not of a dusky color.
Therefore in that which is in these leon flesh not fraudulent nor cancerous, you must make the patient be between your hands and placed in the sunlight, and uncover his nostrils, and prick your own finger in those flesh. And then extract that to the foreparts, and then incise that which you have comprehended of those with a sharp and subtle spatula of one part until you know that all the flesh has been removed; that if there remains of it any cause of which the abscission is possible, then you root that with one of the subtle instruments with facility until of it remains no cause. But if it bleeds or an abscess occurs, then you pause to him what you must; or if it is of the malignant abscesses, then you cut and cauterize that until it is cut off and the cavities are all removed.
And then be put in the nose after the incision a little wine and water or wine. But if the nose is open and from it proceeds humidity into the palate, then you know that it is already healed.
But if the humidity does not penetrate as it should, then you know that from within him is flesh wound in the pus that soars bones of the nostrils to which it has not reached abscission.
Therefore then you must introduce a thread of linen into which there is some thickness, and weave in it moth's wool, and place between each wool the quantity of the finger or less, and engage the patient and introduce one extremity of the thread into the nostril with the ray or with other cause which is to him possible.
And as that will have been done, that he may throw his odor into until it reaches the canals of the nostrils, and be spit upon his throat, because troops of times the resemblance to this action do the children in the schools, and it is lighter cause to him who wants to do it.
And then pause the two extremities of the thread, one extremity which issues over the nose and the other which remains in the nose, and then administer a lock of flesh with the wools that are in the thread, and do this until you know that the flesh is already among the wools of the thread.
And then extract the thread, and pause in the nose after the abstraction of the blood a poultice, and do this for three days or more until the ointment corrodes all that is remaining of the flesh.
And then at the end of the cause, pause in the nose a tube of lead for some days until it is healed.
But if you desire of cure that which requires, use of that.
And this is the form of the instrument to capipurge maker with which oils and medicines are distilled in the nostrils:
And make it of silver or of iron, which is similar to a small open lamp, thus as a small conch, and the meat similarly.
And if you wish, make a closed tube like a pipe, and the tube of the instrument to be used for purging be flat, uncovered; to which have a handle at the back of it, with which you hold it when you pour into it oil or water as you wish of the suckable causes.
Chapter XXV.
Of the ills in the extremities of the nose.
Many times the pain in the extremities of the nose is manifested, and is magnified and lamented on some days, when it is not seen to be looked after.
And for that reason, you should investigate that at the beginning of its appearance, and eradicate all of it. And then place on the spot a cautery or a medicine that is burning, the one that is in place of it.
But if the incision is delayed until it is magnified, then consider if it is calcified, hard, of a dark color, and of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron for it is a dangerous abscess; for many times the one who incides this abscess must endure great malice from the one who had it.
And if the abscess is of a lion's touch and not of a dark color, and sometimes when incision is possible in all of it, then evacuate the patient and incise it without fear, and cure the spot with water that exudes and constrict within that it be healed.
Chapter XXVI.
Of suturing the nose and the lips and the ear when the continuity is dissolved by plague or by similar things.
Know that when an accident occurs dissolving continuity in one of these cartilages, pay little confidence in that operation unless in some men.
Therefore, when it becomes necessary for anyone to have any of these causes, consider if it is fresh plague with its blood, and then you adjust the two lips of the plague with suture, and then take care of it until it is healed.
And if the lips of the dissolved continuity are already separated, and each is made healthy, then you must scrape each part of its apparent edge until blood comes out. And then adjust the two lips with suture and strengthen them, and over the powder sprinkle dragon's blood and a thin layer of resin, and place over the powder a piece of diaphana plaster, or some other of the consolidating plasters, and leave that tied for two or three days, and then untie it and exchange that plaster and leave it until the wounds are by themselves closed, and then take care with an enema until it is healed.
But the manner of suturing is that you add the dissolved continuity or with needles as we have recounted in the suturing of the belly, or add the dissolved continuity with thread as you have done and have known.
Chapter XXVII.
Of the extraction of those causes that come in the two lips in the parts between them.
Many times it becomes necessary for many men in the parts between their lips some abscesses hard like fat of worms, and some of them are smaller and some are larger.
Therefore, when you convert the lips and split each of those hard things completely, and then incise the abscess, fill the place with dragon's blood until the blood is restrained, and then wash it with vinegar and cure the place with water that is astringent, until it is healed.
Chapter XXVIII.
Of incising the flesh adjusted in the gums.
Greatly often there is a growth on the gum, flesh adjusted, which the ancients called an albulus, therefore, when you suspend that with tongs or have it with the forceps and incise it, you must cut its root, and let the blood run.
And then place on the spot dragon's blood or other astringent or drying powders.
And if that flesh returns, then incise it again, and cauterize it, for then the cautery will not return.
Chapter XXIX.
Of the reason of teeth with iron.
When on the surface of the teeth of the parts between them and of the front and between the gums are adjusted rough, jagged, and some times are of black and are made yellow or green while the gum feels for this corruption and are made the teeth jagged.
And therefore, when you make the patient sit between your hands and place the head of him in your lap, and scrape the teeth in which appear those rough things and causes resembling sand until none of them remain, and this do of the blackness and of the yellowness and of the others until they are modified.
And therefore, if it is last that which is in those of the beginning of the root, it is good; and if not, then you iterate the root over those on the other day and the second and the third until it comes to the last statement in that which you want.
And know that the teeth have need of drills of diverse forms and of diverse figures according to how it is prepared for your operation. And because the razors which the tooth is scraped from the inside are other than the razors which are scraped between the teeth according to other forms, and these forms of razors you must prepare as you shall see forthwith:
Chapter .xxx.
Of the Eradication of Teeth.
Know that you cure the tooth of its pain with all diligence and take your time in its complete eradication, for there is no cause that should supplant the healing of it when it is eradicated, for its substance sublimates within that excuse in the eradication of it.
But know when the patient is forced to have that tooth eradicated, that you must firmly certify which tooth is the painful one, for often the pain deceives the patient and leads you to believe it is in a healthy tooth, and you eradicate that one and the pain does not cease until the bad and painful tooth is eradicated, for we have already seen this by the operation of the barbers.
Therefore, as you must be certain which tooth is the painful one, and that you know well, then know that you must scarify in the circuit of the tooth with a spatula in which there is some virtue, until it is dissolved from the tooth of the gum on all sides, and then with those words, or with subtle forceps at the beginning little by little until that concucesquas.
And then, with a strong grip, hold the large forceps for good communication or great stupor, and place the head of the patient between your teeth, which you hold well so that it does not harm, and then draw the tooth according to straightness in a manner that you do not break it, nor give the patient greater pain.
And therefore if it is not forgotten, then take one of those instruments, and place that one below it on all sides with ease and exert the removal of it thus that it is done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is broken or corroded, then know that you must compress of cloth that break and tighten that with the extremity of a fine ray so that it not be broken in the hour of your constriction upon that with forceps.
And know that you work exquisitely with scarification in the circuit of all parts of the gum and guard well your strength that you do not break that and remain part of it, and return upon the patient for the malice that be greater than the first pain of it.
And guard yourself that you do not do that which some ignorant barbers do in their fistinacio and audacity upon the eradication of theirs, for they do not administer what we have recommended; for often times they bring upon men maladies great ones which are more difficult to be broken, and the roots of them remaugulated all, or some of those, or that you extract that with some bones of the mandible as well as many times we have testified.
And after the eradication of it, the mouth be washed with wine caut or wine agre with salt.
And if it behoves to flow of blood thereby, as often times it behoves, then apply a certain quantity of zegi and sprinkle it upon the wound, and if you do not confer that zegi, cauterize.
The form of the forceps and subtle forceps with which the tooth is mauled at the beginning be of long extremity, of short handle and thick, so that they not be bent when with those you must work.
And be as times of thick handle so that when you tighten with those they not be bent, be short extremities.
And be made of Indian iron descentment made of straight extremities, and in the extremities of those be teeth of which some introne in the others and tighten by strong constriction descent, and some times the extremities of those be the form of the beak of a bird the one which has name ciconia, so it is gaunt, and they are of strong constriction.
Chapter .xxxi.
Of the Eradication of Teeth and the Extraction of the Bones of the Cracked Mandibles.
When you must the eradication of a tooth which is broken remain some cause, then know that you must place upon the location a poultice with border for a day or for two until the location be mollified; and then with some instruments or forceps the extremities of which are assembled to the beak of a bird called ciconia or gaunt, the form of the forceps:
The extremities of those be made from within as a file or rasp.
And if you do not obey to your easement with these forceps or those, then know that you must cave upon the root and scrape all the flesh and insert the instrument the one which has name atali, so it is a small lever of which the form is this:
And be of short extremity thick a little, and not be bent so that it not be broken.
Therefore if by that the root be broken, well be it; and if not, help yourself with these other instruments of which these are the forms: the form of the first instrument be of triangular extremity in which there be some thickness:
The form of the second instrument be that it be triangular and of more subtle extremity.
And already so helped with this instrument having two ramps of which this is the form near the following: And with other instruments the ones which I shall precede in the rasping of teeth; for the scraping is made with this instrument the one which is assembled to a large onion, and this is the form:
Of the triangular limb twisted or short, which is some thickness, and not enclosed so that it is not squeezed.
And know that the instruments of the moving teeth are so and similarly the other instruments.
But the artificer skilled and subtle in the art, finds for himself according to what to him signifies the operation and the diverse ailments; because they are of the ailments to which the ancients did not say nor pause proper instruments, for the forms of diverse species.
But if the bone of the jaw or of the other bones of the mouth is fractured, or if it may be, then let it be cured on that in its place with what is convenient to it of the instruments and the forceps which we have said in the extraction of the roots of the teeth, and help with the gesture of which this is the form:
And let there be in it some thickness little by little, and be enclosed or held with the mouth so that it does not escape or flee until the bone of all is set; and then restore the place with medicines convenient to it.
But if in the bone is a small puncture, then root that of that puncture and of its blackness, and cure that until it is healed.
Chapter .xxxii.
Of the cure of the teeth eminent above the others.
When the teeth are eminent not according to their natural course, for those the form is laid, and mostly when it happens to women, and mostly to the venerable old ones; therefore, because you consider: if a tooth is nothing near another tooth, and it is not possible to suture or liniment it, then root that; but that it is not annexed to another tooth, then you incise it with this instrument of which this is the form; and it is similar to a pig's snout, and be made of Indian iron of a sharp extramitat.
And let your incision be with which you incise it in several days for the hardness of the tooth, and that it not be gnawed by another of the teeth.
And if the eminent tooth is exposed to filing, then file that with a file of Indian iron of which this is the form:
And let it all be of Indian iron and the margin well-made; and be of small sharp points as a file with which needles are made, with which the tooth be filed little by little in several days with facility, so that no other tooth be gnawed and broken. And then line that at the end, and root that with some razors.
And if the tooth of which a part is fractured and it pricks the tongue, then cover that until the sharpness of that fracture is stayed and smoothed, and be filled so that the tongue does not prick it nor the word be corrupted.
Chapter .xxxiii.
Of the restoration of teeth marred with filings of gold or silver.
When accidents happen to the teeth in front with concussion and removal by percussion or by fall, and the patient cannot strengthen over that which he eats, and you have cured that with stiptatic medicines, and it has not been of any avail, then because it does not break, it is made in those that are strengthened with filings of gold and not of silver, because silver becomes green and can be seen after several days, but gold at no time is changed.
And let the filings be in such subtlety and thickness according to the quantity that it can enter between the teeth; and the form of the reccio is that you take the filing and take the double of it between two healthy teeth, and then that you curve it with two tortuosities of the filing between two marred ones, or if it is one or several, until it reaches the healthy tooth of the other side. And then iterate the teyssiment into the part from which you began, and strengthen your hand with facility and skill so that it is not marred.
And let your striccio with which you strengthen the filings be the roots of the teeth so that it does not escape.
And then incise the superfluous extremities of the filing with forceps or tosoys, and add those in each place with gesture, and convert them and hide them between the healthy tooth and the marred one, so that it does not make injury to the tongue. And then let it be laid so tightly like a Roman.
But if it is loosened or broken, strengthen that or those with other filings in such a manner in all their time.
And this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the rection of two healthy teeth and two marred ones, as well as sometimes these are tied:
And when it is done that a tooth or two are returned to their places after the fall of each one, and they are recurssed as we have recounted, and that they remain marred.
And that is done only by a good artificer and wise.
And sometimes it is fitted some cause of the bones of the cow, and it is made as the form of a tooth, and it is placed in the place where the tooth is missing, and it is strengthened as we have said, and remains and serves with it for a long time.
Chapter .xxxiv.
Of the incision of the ligament which comes in the tongue and prohibits speech.
This ligament which comes from the tongue some times or is natural with which man is born, or accidental and happens by plague which is already consolidated.
And the operation on him is that men open the mouth of the patient, his head existing in the tieu se; and raise his tongue, and then cut that ligament nerve according to the latitude within which the tongue is released from its recess.
But if in that there is any hardness or knot, and that is due to the consolidation of gout, then you throw an oil and cut that according to the latitude within which you have incised the ligament and the knot is dissolved.
And guard yourself that no fissure be made in the flesh of the chin and that you cut here artery and blood comes.
And then wash the traces of the incision with water or with wine or with cold water; and then place the tongue moistened; so it is the way which has the patient to keep the tongue in any night so that it is not consolidated again.
But if there occurs a flow of blood, place on the location vitriol trissat; but if the blood comes out, then cauterize the location with a cautery  which is convenient for this. And that cure with the other causes within which it is healed.
Chapter XXXV.
Of the extraction of a ranula under the tongue.
Sometimes it happens under the tongue an abscess resembling a small lump that prevents the tongue from its natural operation; and often it is magnified within which it swells the mouth.
And the operation on him is that men open the mouth of the patient sensing in front of the sun and consider the abscess.
And if you see it of a dark color or of black, hard, to which the patient does not feel sensation, then do not touch that because it is gangrenous.
And if it is inclined to whiteness, in which there is humidity, then you put the oil in it, and cut it with a subtle spatula, and cut it from every part; and if blood comes to you in the hour of your operation, then you place above  zegi trissat, that is vitriol, within which it is restricted the blood.
And then return to your work within which you had treated it with compliment of it, within which it is washed with wine and salt; and cure that with the other cure with water within which it is healed.
Chapter XXXVI.
Of the extraction of an abscess of the ears and of that which is nothing in the throat and of the other abscesses.
When in the throat it is swollen, so are the glands which are assembled swollen, which sometimes happen outwards and are called boils, which when you cure them with water that we have said in the division and it is not healed, then you consider if the abscess is hard, of a dark color, of little sensation, then do not touch that with iron.
And if it is of a reddish color and the root is thick, then do not touch that with iron because of the flow of blood; let it be left within which it is matured, and then either you will extract that, or it will be ruptured by itself.
And if it is of a white color, radon, and the root of it is subtle, then that is that which must be incised.
And the operation on it is that you consider, before your operation, if the abscess has already rested it with a complete rest or if it is diminished with some diminution; and then make the patient stand before the sun, and his head be in the tieu se, and open the mouth of him, and the servant takes between his hands pressing the tongue of him from with a noble instrument of which this is the form:
And it is made of silver or of brass, and it is subtle like a knife.
Therefore, as you press with that the tongue and it is shown to you the abscess, and gaze upon that with your eyesight, then take oil and put that in the opening, and pull that to the parts outwards as much as you can. And other water that you pull any cause of the tunics, and then cut that with the instrument of which this is the form:
And other water that you pull any cause of the tunics, and then cut that with the instrument of which this is the form: And it is assembled to forceps, however the extremities of it are curved, so that the orifice of each one is in the right of the other, very sharp, which be of iron indi embedded.
But if this instrument is not to you present, then cut that with a spatula of which this is the form of it: And it is sharp on one part, not sharp on the other part.
And since you have incised a furrow, cut the other according to this same manner of incision, and then the incision the patient gargles with cold water
But if it happens a flow of blood, gargle with water of decoction of the bark of  millefolium or of myrtle leaf and similar to that of the stiptic causes within which the flow of blood is restricted, and then cure that within which it is healed.
And sometimes naysso in the throat other abscesses other than those boils, and cut those according to what I have said in the incision of two furrows equally.
And I have already treated a woman of an abscess which was in the throat of her, which abscess tended to a dark color, of little sensation, which had already closed the throat of her, and the woman breathed with tight meat, and had already prohibited to her eating and drinking of water, and she had already arrived at death if may it had stayed for a day or for two.
And the abscess had grown so much that for two months there were two openings through which it came out.
So I cut it fistularly and stayed in one of the openings, and pulled out that one, and it came out a large portion, and then I cut that one which I understood from the other opening, and then I opened the mouth of it, and I compressed its tongue, and then I stayed the opening in that abscess.
And then I drained a large portion of it, and it was not running from it except a little blood. Therefore, the abscess of that woman was completely drained, and she immediately began to drink water and eat soft food, so I did not stop cutting into that abscess many times for a long time, and abscesses would succeed in its place, which incision would extend as long as it was.
Therefore, I inserted a needle and cauterized the opening of it, so as to prevent further addition; and then I walked around and I did not know what God had done with that, from that time.
Chapter .xxxvii.
Of incision of a boil when it is abscesses.
When a catarr arises on the boil, and it is abscesses and it is long, then it is called perpendicular; and if it is in the part below thick and round, and then it is called a bubo.
But when it is cured with what we have said in the division, and it does not compare to your cure, and then sometimes that abscess cauterized already is gone from it and it is subtle, then you should cut into that which is added round; and if it is to that length, and it is bloody, of brown color or black, and it is not to the touch, then you should attempt the incision of it, because in that there is fear about the patient.
And when you see that according to the manner that I have said of its whiteness and length, that you should make the patient lie down and press the tongue of it with an instrument of which you process its shape and then place the opening in the navel, and pull that down and cut into it with one of the two instruments which are said in the incision of two mills.
And you should not cut into it unless it is adjusted over the natural term of its addition, because if you cut into it more, you will damage its speaking.
And after the incision, use that which has been recommended in the incision of two mills, and cure that while it is healing.
But if the patient was frightened by the incision of it, then you should use a needle in the cauterization of it, and the manner of the cautery in it is not but with a sharp water, and it is that you place the head of the patient in your side, and then press the tongue of it with the instrument which we have said, and then take from the water which we have said in the chapter of cauterization, and apply it with that living cause, and place it not thick nor subtle, and from that fill the concavity of the instrument of which this is the shape:
Let the extramitat of its concavity in which the medicine is placed be like the concavity of a spoon of ray, and place the instrument with the medicine on the wound, and the patient yawns on his side so that saliva or mucus of the mouth of that flows through the intrinsic medicine, so that it does not descend from it for any cause over the opening of it and that it is covered.
And then with your hand on the medicine, and express it on the uvula for the space of half an hour until you see it being darkened and sedated by the bite of the medicine.
And if you want, take a cotton and envelop it over the extremity of the ray, and submerge the cotton in the medicine, and introduce the ray with the cotton into a tube of above until the cotton adheres to that tube, and do this as many times until you achieve what you want from the cauterization of the uvula, and then remove it when it dries and falls after about three days or four.
And if you wished to repeat the medicine, repeat it, and after the cauterization, cleanse the circuit of the uvula with cotton dipped in border, and modify it with that which is in the circuit of it of the medicine, and be washed with cold water, and be cured from then on with embrocation, and give gargles until it is healed.
And this kind of cure is more safe than incision and more long of fear.
Sometimes the uvula is cured with that which is more subtle than cauterization and incision, because it is cured with fumigation in this manner: take calamine, hyssop, oregano, rue, siccated arabic, chamomile, broyda and similar to those of the herbs, and adjust all of those causes, or some of them, in an olla, and they be submerged in strong wine, and boil; and the olla be well washed with decent lut, and be in the middle of the olla a hole, on which be placed an instrument concave of brass according to this manner; be made of silver or of brass.
And be introduced the extremity into the mouth of the patient until the vapor reaches the uvula on the concha, until the uvula be somewhat obscured.
And then repeat over it many times until it is dry, and guard yourself that you do not do this cure at the beginning of the coming of abscesses, because it would too much adjust in the abscess, and do not do that, but you must declare the abscess of it cauterized.
But if you do not have this instrument at present, then take a cane and compose in the middle of it a cup of wool, so that the mouth of the patient is covered, because the wool cup prohibits the vapor from burning the mouth.
And this cure is good for health.
Chapter XXXVIII.
Of the extraction of thorns and of what adheres in the throat and of the other causes.
Many things, stuck in the throat, or thorns or any other cause.
Therefore, you must extract what of those appears, on which the gaze falls, because you press the tongue with an instrument beforehand, so that to you is declared what is in the throat.
And what does not appear and is to you hidden in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach, because forth, the cause annexed to the throat is thrown-up by vomiting; or make the patient swallow a piece of bread or a root of lettuce or a piece of dry bread; or prepare a piece of dry sea sponge, and tie that firmly with thread, and then make the patient swallow that, because when it arrives at the place in which the thorns are and are extracted, then they are thrown-up. And yet take an eel and tie it firmly with thread, and its head is placed and its tail is extracted; or take a porcupine and its quills and its tail are extracted.
But if they are not thrown-up with those causes which we have said, then use an instrument of lead according to this form:
And it should be thicker than a ray, and in the middle of it there is a concavity which you introduce into the throat with ease.
And hold its head elevated upwards, and guard that the touching of its bone of the throat, so that it may be moved to its body and with that which pushes the bone or the thorn, or that the physician with his hand.
But however, that the patient that is introduced is milder, for the science of the place of the annexed cause and pushes it down, and pulls his hand with the instrument upwards, all that according to the quantity which is prepared to him before it is thrown-up.
Chapter XXXIX.
Of the extraction of blood stuck in the throat.
When blood is medicated with what we have said in the division of the cure with medicines and does not conform, consider then in the throat of the patient to the sun, because you have examined the tongue of him with the instrument which to you we have recommended.
Therefore, if you see the blood, extract that with a small onci or with subtle gestures decently.
And if it is not possible to extract with that, then take a concave cannula and introduce that into the throat of the patient, and then place in the concavity of the cannula a burning iron, and do this as many times (until the blood is dead and is removed from the throat) and abstain the patient all day from water.
And then prepare a vessel full of cold water, and work the mouth of him in that, and wash the mouth with that; and do not swallow any of that, and evil the water one hour after another with his hand, because the blood as soon as it feels the water catches.
But if it is not thrown-up with what we have recommended, then subfumigate the patient with thyme or with asafoetida by the instrument which we have recommended in the subfumigation of the uvula.
Do this, so that it may fall.
And there is another way of operation in the subfumigation of that, which is that you take a bowl in which there are burning coals and the bowl is covered with a cover in the middle of which there is a hole, and it is composed in that hole the extremity of the instrument; and then let the subfumigation go down; and place the patient's mouth on the extremity of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the subfumigation is not thrown-up until you know that the subfumigation has arrived at the blood, because the blood as soon as it feels the subfumigation falls.
And if it does not catch, then you iterate the subfumigation many times, and abstain the patient from drinking, and eat salty and spicy foods, and do not drink water, and thus it is necessary that with this regimen it be thrown-up.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the blood of the throat is treated when it is seen; and it is similar to forceps as you see, except that in it there is some curvature: which is placed in the throat, and the extremity of it is similar to the beak of a stork, which is gripped, in which it is sharpened with a file, so that, when grasping any cause, it does not let go.
Chapter XL.
In which is the sum of the sermon on the appearance of abscesses and in their section.
Abscesses are many species, of many manners, according to what we remember of them, of each one in this book.
And they are diverse in perforation and section of them by two manners, of which one is by the species of abscesses in themselves; and by that which we grasp of the humidities.
And the second way is for the places where boils occur in the body, because the boil that occurs on the head is different from the boil that occurs on the buttocks; and the boil that occurs in the fleshy place is different from the boil that occurs in the joint; and each of them has its own treatment by operation.
And more boils there are some that should not be pierced but rather allowed to mature by the body's own healing or by the completion of their course.
And other boils that should be drained when they are ripe, and not allowed to mature by their own course, such as boils that occur near the joints, because when a boil occurs near a joint, its being there is prolonged until the pus that is in the circuit of it is discharged, and then the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, so that it causes contraction of that limb; or it is a boil near the main member, and if you delay the drainage of it until its maturity, it will cause harm to the main member; or it is near the buttocks, therefore perforate it before it matures; and you should not perforate it crudely, before its proper digestion, but the one that is near the buttocks, so that you cannot reach the perineum of it and prolong it to the parts behind the buttocks, and make a fistula, or that it be done in a way that it is not healed. But more importantly, you should know the time of the boil's drainage, and that is when it is mature.
And know that it is mature when there is a cessation of pain and fever, and with the decrease of the redness and pulse, and the sharpness of the head of the boil, and the other signs.
And that you should know that the drainage should be done in the place pus is coming from the boil and from the pus coming from the healing of the eminence.
And the incision should always be made along the length of the flesh or the body, whether the boils are in the parts of the limbs or the feet, and in the places of the tendons, of the nerves, of the arteries; and, lastly, in all places equal to those in which there is no reflection; because in those that are reflected, use the incision according to that limb.
But when the boil is in a fleshy place, then it is best to let the incision be made after its digestion has been confirmed according to its course, as we have said; because if you perforate it before that, the course of the pus is prolonged and a lot of dirt is produced, and then the lips of it are hardened and the depth of it is increased.
But some boils should be incised according to the width of the flesh or the body as necessity demands, or according to what the limb requires.
And you should administer a small incision in small boils, a large and wide or multiple sections in large boils according to the diversity of the size of the boils.
And others are of boils in which the incision should be concave and incised when it is made so that it becomes a pan and it is done in a way that it already adheres, like those that occur in groups of boils and buboes.
And of those there are those that are incised with a section having three angles; and of those there are those that are incised in the way that resembles the shape of a myrtle leaf, like the boils of the armpits.
And of those there are those in which a round incision and a lunar incision, and those similar to them, are administered.
But that one to which there is no such as his boils are superficial, you should perforate it with a superficial incision, or a flat one only.
And when the boil is large and has already collected a lot of pus, that you perforate it and do not attempt to extract all the pus in that hour; having extracted one part of it, and then close the boil until the next day, and then extract a larger part, and so do this several times according to the degree until it is completely drained.
And especially if the patient is of frail virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old person in decrepitude, because the animal spirit is often resolved with the exit of the pus, and then the patient may die, and you should operate on them with caution.
And guard this chapter with great care, and in the way you perforate these boils, you should abstain from the plagues and consider therefore whether the plague of the boil is small, or a flat section, then you should administer the poultices of it or of a counter-irritant; and if the boil is large, and the fissures of the incision are many, then you should place a piece of cloth in each one until they meet.
And if in the boil a part of the skin is cut off or has been concaved in the circuit, then you should cover it with a piece of old cloth or a thread made of linen, as when you have treated pans or abscesses, with its humidity; and strengthen this on the third day; and then process this and care for it with what is necessary until it is healed.
But if there occurs a flow of blood during the operation, then you should administer cold water and vinegar in which you have soaked a piece of linen, and place this over the place of the blood flow several times.
But if the flow of blood persists, then you should administer a regimen and cure and powders which I have recommended in many places of this our book and of division.
But if it is in wintertime, and the place of the abscess is a place of numb nerves, then you should infuse powders in wine and oil, and place those on the places.
And if it is in summer, and the places are fleshy, then you should place powders mixed with water and oil or with wine and oil, and all that be applied until the third day, as we have said, and then you should open the abscess and cleanse it and administer to its cure what is convenient to it until it is healed.
And thus is what is necessary of the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally, but according to the way of distinction I have already said of every abscess in what manner is the way of its cure by chapters individually.
Chapter .xli.
Of the section of abscesses which come in the nape of the neck.
In the nape of the neck, small abscesses appear, and they are of a kind of nodes which contain tunics that are to their making; and the kinds of them are many.
And of them are pimples, and of those it is that contain humidity similar to lime. And of those are the ones that contain humidity similar to dust, and resembling to them; and of those are the ones that are stony, hard.
And in the section of all of them, and in the extraction of those there is no fear, as you must the exterior of those does not make contrary artery.
And the operation in section of those is that you probe those with an instrument the shape of which comes near thus, which is called entromes, as long as you know that it contains.
Because if that which contains is humidity, then you should divide that with section according to the length by superficial section according to this form:
And begins in the section of the line of .B. into the line of .G. Therefore, as the humidity is evacuated, then you excoriate that skin that contains that humidity, and do not leave of that any cause of all, because troops once gone back, if there remain of that any cause.
And then you submerge the wound in Egyptian wash, if it is present, and if not, in water and salt; and fill with that the wound and leave it for another day, because with that you corrode all that is broken of that skin.
And then repeat on that wound with Egyptian wash second and third time if you need it, until you are confident that there is no longer any cause of that skin; then cure the wound with wash until it is healed.
And if the abscess contains fatty nodes, then you should cut that according to this form: with a section having the shape of a cross, and get onces between the two lips of the section and scrape that from all parts, and exert your strength in the extraction of the tunic which contains that.
But if to your artery makes opposition, then do what I have told you first.
And similarly do in the stony abscess of section and cure according to what we have told you; and section on a stony abscess is easier, because it is of little blood and of little humidity.
And sometimes there are some of these abscesses which are in the head of some men with which there is no humidity at all; the cause of which is because I incised upon an abscess in the head of an old woman and brought the abscess back as a hard, rough, white sore, which could not be pierced, and if anyone was struck with that, it would plague them.
But in the other abscesses accidents in the head other than this is not this chapter, as well as the abscesses that come to the heads of children and you must the roots of the ears, but the section of all these is superficial.

Chapter .xlii.
Of the section of scrophulas which happen in the neck.
Many times these abscesses become in the neck and in the armpits and in the groin; and sometimes they happen in the other parts of the body.

And it is more caution that the vein or nerve is not cut.

When the blood is separated.

And then fill the wound with old cloth which you have already submerged in Egyptian ointment, and then cure it.
And if you cut that abscess entirely, then cover it so that you adjust the two lips of the wound and close it as soon as pus comes out so that there is no superfluous discharge.
But if you see that there is an excess of discharge due to the size of the abscess, cover it so that you understand to cut the root of it, and remove it and administer suture and what is said.
And those of the abscesses that contain humidity, perforate it with a superficial perforation where you see the place of maturation of it, and place a perforation of it so that the pus flows from the lower part of the body, as we have said.
And then administer the perforation, washes with ointment and similar things to those, so that it corrodes what is coming from the corruption. And then when you see the wound already cleaned, then cure it with ointment of generative flesh until it is healed.
Chapter XLIII.
Of the incision of the abscess of the boil within the groin.
The ancients said this incision in the groin, and I have not seen any man in our land that it has been done.
And this is the inscription of the sermon of those.
But in men having a hernia, cover that the extraction of the groin be avoided, as for that it is not well done for their sake because all the veins and major arteries of the body are here.
But in those who have abscesses caused in the mouth or groin or both ears, when the illness is not in the canal, cover that you use the incision of the groin to avoid the damage which is done by perforation.
Therefore, cover that when we want this, that they cut the groin below three circles of the circles of the groin, or four with a small incision for the latitude in that which is between two circles by quantity, that the incision be in the fascia, not in the cartilage, and this place is convenient for incision, because it is deprived of flesh and the vessels of blood of it are there.
And if the physician is fearful, cover that he extends the groin with an incision, and then open the groin until it reaches the canal, but avoid the blood vessels if you see any cause of them.
And then cut the fascia according to what we have recommended; and it is significant on the incision of the canal by the flame which is of that exit with what is of it disrupted and by the abscess of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
Therefore, as the hour is renewed in which perforation is feared, add two lips of the groin of the wound, and stitch it alone if it is the cartilage.
And then administer medicines that make flesh grow until it is healed.
And Albucasis says that the sum of the sermon which we have recommended, the exposition is not but that you see that some of these abscesses have already opened the groin of the patient, and the patient has come into death, and the ale of it is dried up, and some go to cut the epiglottis so that the patient breathes over the place of the wound for some respiration, and be saved from death.
And for that reason, I command to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is consumed; and the malice of it is for three days; and then cover that you close the wound, and cure it until it is healed.
And that which I have seen with my own eyes, is that a servant took a knife and placed it in his groin and cut with it a part of the canal of the lung, and I was called to the cure of him, and I brought back the woman as it is mooed of the dead, and I uncovered the wound and brought back the blood which was coming out of the wound small.
Therefore, I was confessed that he had not cut a vein nor guided it, and the wind was coming out of the wound, and I cured it until it was healed.
And I did not accuse the servant if not for the voice, and after some days returned to the improvement of his dispositions.
And now I say that in the section of the epileptic there is no fear.
Chapter XLIV.
Of incision over an abscess which happens in the throat outside, and is called a hernia of the throat.
This abscess called a hernia of the throat is a large abscess according to the color of the body, and it moves in women.
And it is according to two ways, whether it is natural or accidental.
And in the natural one it is not a matter of curing.
And the accidental one is according to two ways, one of which is similar to fatty nodes, and the other way is similar to an abscess that is made by the blockage of an artery, and in that one there is fear. And no cove that it be made presumption to it, like iron, but in that which is small. Chapter XLV.
Of incision of the species of nodes.
Of nodes there are many species and I have already said all the species of them in the division.
And I must recount as the difference between a node and an excrescence as if making a doubt.
Therefore, I say that in an excrescence there is heat and fever and violent pains until the boiling of the superfluity is stopped; and it is a putrefaction that then ceases the fever, the pain, and the heat.
But in a node there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains that which is in the sac proper to it.
And it is according to the color of the body, and its beginning is like a cyst and it is made so as a vacuum, whether it is larger or smaller, and they are according to two species, whether they are fatty and contain humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, according to what I said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the cure of a node, that you examine it and inquire about it at the beginning with the instrument that is called intromes, according to how it will come its form in the chapter which is near this.
And the manner of inquiry of abscesses and of all nodes, and it is that you take this instrument and introduce it into the place most humid which you find in the abscess, and you revolve your said ones with that little by little until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the core.
And then last your hand according to the measure of the greatness of the abscess, and then extract the intromes and consider what is issued in the trace of it.
And if the humidity is flowing out, of whatever color it may be, then you incise it with a superficial incision according to what I have said in the other abscesses.
And if from the trace of the intromes there is no humidity, then you know that it is fatty.
And dry over it with an incision having the shape of a cross according to this form: as such as I have taught you, and suspend that with tweezers, and excoriate the core from all parts with ease, and keep the skin or sac, if you can, over it and extract that sania with the node.
But if it is broken in the operation, it is not possible to extract that sania, and many times it must be so, and then you extract it in pieces until there remains no cause from it.
Because if from it remains no cause, little or much, the node returns according to the most.
And if you see that from it remains any small part, then fill the wound with some sharp and corrosive powders and strengthen the wound, and place on it a cautery of the abscess, and cure it with the other cure until it is healed.
And if it is a large node, then you sew the two lips of it and cure it with what is necessary for healing.
But if a pulsatile vein is to it contrary, or non-pulsatile, then you cauterize and fill the place of a zegi three times that is vitriol and leave it straight for two days or three until you can scar the wound and that it rests the boiling of the blood; and then return to incise that which is broken from the node.

Chapter .xlvii.

Chapter .xlix.
Of the section of abscesses that happen because of artery or vein.
When an artery is ruptured, and the cord which is above it is consolidated, then many times abscesses happen. And the signs by which it is known that inflammation and abscess are from the artery or vein: that when an abscess is from the artery it is long aggregated in the front of the body; and that when you press the abscess with your fingers, you feel in it that which is stridor.
And that which is from the vein is round to the manifest of the body.
And the section on this abscess is an error, and most of all in that which is below the armpits, and in the corners, and in the neck, and in many places of the body; and it is very large, therefore it is necessary to avoid its cure with iron, and that which is in the extremities, or on the head, it is necessary to avoid.
But on that which is of those by inflammation of the orifice of the artery, cut a section in the cord, in the long; and then scrape the section with hooks, and then the artery, and deliver from the tunics until it is uncovered.
And then put on that needle and make it penetrate into the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, — which causes you to ease in the extraction of two arteries which are in the temples.
And then prick the place which is between two ligaments with a spatula until the blood that is in it is removed, and the abscess is dissolved.
And then administer a cure in which it is engendered power until the ligaments fall; and then take care of it with suitable ointments to it until it is healed.
And if the abscess is from the section of a vein, then it is necessary for you to have with your hand that which is possible of the abscess with the cord, and then introduce the needle below the place which you have had below your hand, and make it penetrate; and be in that double thread until you extract it from the other side, and then tie the abscess with a good ligament according to what I have told you in the ligament of the grape of two parts with two extremities of the thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be extracted, then introduce the thread with that needle below the whole abscess, from the incision of the first needle, and tighten your threads in four places.
Then dry the abscess in the middle place of it until when it is emitted that which is in it, then you cut the superfluity of the cord, and leave that which of it is tied.
And then place on it the powder which you have soaked in wine and oil, and then administer the cure which is made with warm and damp cloths while it is healing.
Chapter 1 of the abscess which occurs due to a twisting of nerves.
Thus as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, and similarly abscesses occur in nerves when they are struck or overworked, and by similar means.
And it is made most in the places of the arms or the ankle, or in any place where the joints are bad.
And it is a serious abscess, and it is similar in color to the rest of the body, and in the majority of its dispositions it is painful and when it is tightened with violence, the patient feels like a stupor.
And it is not an abscess that is attached in the front of the body, and for this reason the chain is left, and it is bad in every part and does not go to the parts in front or behind.
Therefore, those that are in the joints should not be enclosed with iron, because it will very much increase contraction.
But those that are in the head or on the forehead, bind with a spatula. But if it is a small abscess, then take it with the forceps and cut it from the root.
And if it is large, then you suspend it with a hook, and scrape it, and then put it back; and adjust the wound with suture, and care for it until it is healed.
Chapter 2.
Of the incision of an abscess that occurs from a boil that occurs in the belly.
And it happens to some men, growths in the bellies of those and in other parts of the body of those, which are called fungals because of their resemblance to fungi, of which the root is subtle and the head of it is thick; and already the lips of those are converted, and it is of those that is small, and it is of those that is very magnified.
And I have already seen one, and in the belly of him there were two parts which were more like fungi, and there was no difference between them, white, of fine root.
And already the lips of those were reversed and were splitting, and moisture was running from it all the time.
Therefore, I incised those and took out of one in a weight of eighteen ounces. and the other, six ounces.

And then adjust in the tightness of the leaden thread; therefore, do not cease to strengthen the lead greatly, until it is cut off and falls by itself through its work.
But if the boil is of thick root, then in the incision of it there is some cause of fear and of terror, and more so in that which is in the belly.
But it is possible that you should incise the majority of it, and then cauterize it so that it does not return.
And then care for it until the wound is healed.
And guard yourself that you do not presume to incise those that are of dusky color, of little feeling, of little regard, because those are cancerous abscesses.

Chapter 3.
Of the cure of an eminence of the navel.
Eminence of the navel is made by many causes; or by fissures of the skin which is on the belly, and from which the cloth or intestine comes out according to how it should be in the other ruptures; or by blood which flows from a vein or artery according to what has been said before, or by wind contracted in it.
But if it is by a fissure of the skin and by the protrusion of the cloth, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body; and it is lean in pain, and then appears of different situations. And if it is by the egress of the intestine, then the situation of it with that which we have recounted, of greater and diverse variety, and when you press it with your fingers, it is hidden, and then returns; and very much is felt in it, and it is magnified a great deal by the introduction of baths and violent labor.
But if it is by humidity, then it is lean and is not hidden when you press it with your hand, nor is it constricted, nor is it increased.
And if it is by blood, then with these signs appears the abscess in a declining blackness.
But if it is by flesh nothing, then the abscess is serious, thick and hard, and it is placed according to a quantity.
But if it is by wind, then the touch of it is light.
And the operation on him is that you consider at this time if the prominence of the navel is from artery blood, or from vein, or from wind; therefore, if it is prohibited from the cure of him, because in that there is fear and fear as you have been taught in the chapter in which I have said the abscesses by artery and by vein.

And if you have found the cloth, then take that with a finger; and cut the superfluities of it.
But if it is contrary to your artery or vein, then surround that spot, and then return to your operation; and take two needles and put in those two strong threads and introduce two needles in the circuit which you have made around the abscess in a manner of cross, which you make penetrate; and then strengthen the abscess in four parts over the needles.

And if the prominence of the navel is of flesh nothing in it or by humidity, then you must concave the abscess as we have said and extract the blood or the humidity, which you find in it, and then cure that with water which is customary and that consolidates the place.

Chapter LXl.

Chapter LXll.

And count those, whether they are multiplied, one after the other, and are separated by the navel, distinguish those among the ligaments in the navel of each of them. And if some of them are difficult in childbirth and come to what we have said about unnatural figures, then you care for them as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is skillful and does what is done with ease and subtlety, and with delay, and is ingenious according to every figure according to what is prepared for her by the ingenuity bringing to health.
Remembering that which is formed in the womb from embryos and is aborted.
Sometimes they are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and even ten, and it has already been verified that one woman aborted six, and another gave birth to ten, the cause of which was made by the measurement of the glorious wise men.
And all this cove that is in the science of the midwife, that is very important to that appearance of this, and therefore, it is paused to this as much as cove.

Of the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you cure the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of the medicine and it is not outside, and you are forced to use operation with your hand, then you must consider if the woman is of sound virtue and is not among those accidents by which she is feared for loss.
Then you must have the woman lying on her back on her two, and her head inclined down and her thighs raised.
And the minister has those of two parts or is tied on the bed so that the body of him does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you moisten the mouth of the mother with humid oil and mucilage of althea and fennel and the seeds of lily.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucilages, and then she inserts her hand with ease into the mother, and then she searches with her hand in the place where the forceps are in the fetus.
And convenient places in this: therefore you consider if the fetus is prepared that descends on its head, and then you place the forceps in the heels of it, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or in the palate, or below the beard, or in the fork of it, or in the proper places of the back, or below the hypochondria.
But if the descent is on the feet of it, then in the penile, or in the middle of the back.
And you must have the forceps with your right hand, and pause the curvature of it in that place which is between the fingers of your left hand, and insert your hand with ease and place the forceps in one of those places which we have said, until it reaches the left cause.
And then pause and place in the opposite position of it another forceps, or the third if it is necessary, so that the traction is equal, and it is not extension according to its rectum alone.
And may it be good to all parts, so that the delivery of it be eased as it is done in the case of the eradication of it.
And you must in it that which is between them that the extension be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then you must have the midwife anoint some of her fingers with oil and insert them skillfully and revolve with those that are retained.
Therefore, if the part of the fetus is delivered, then the forceps are changed into the place which is most high; and do so until the whole fetus is delivered.
But if the hand is outside the other, and it is not possible to reduce it by the constriction of it, then you must have a cloth wrapped around it; and then extract it until all is delivered, and incise it either at the junction of the hand or in the groin.
And so you must do in the other hand and in the two feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is an accident to it constriction in the delivery, or it is in the head of it water adjusted, then you must insert between the fingers of the scapula spine and split the head and extract the water, or that which describes it with an instrument which is called "alundat", the form of which will come with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter which is next.
And similarly do if the fetus is of a large head by nature: and then you must incise it with the algematu, or that which presses it with the alundat as we have said; and then extract the bones with the forceps.
And if the head is pulled and is constricted by the collarbone, then it is cut so that the moisture which is in the feet be poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor obstructed by the bones, then you cut the head as soon as it is possible to you.
And if the belly's bottom is festering or is in it hydropsy, then you must pierce it so that the moisture which is in it flows out.
But if the thing is on its feet, then the traction of it is lighter and the direction of it to the mouth of the mother is lighter.
But if it is constricted by the belly and the foot, then you must extract it with a cloth which you will have enveloped over your hand, and you will make the belly and the foot so that water runs out of those.
But if the other limbs are stayed and the head is turned, then the midwife puts her left hand in; but if the mouth of the mother is closed, then she puts her hand in the perineum of the mother, and seeks with that the head, and pulls it with the fingers into the mouth of the mother, and then puts in it a hook, or two hooks, and pulls it with those.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted by an abscess caused by a boil, then it must not be operated on; rather, it must be treated with an infusion of humid, fatty causes. And administer plasters; and follow the patient in waters that soften and moisten.
And if the thing is on the side of the body, then if it is possible, it should be lanced; and it should be administered with the water that we have said in the living fetus.
And if that is not possible, then it should be incised in pieces, and extracted.
And you must leave no cause of the second birth.
And when you have completed your entire operation, then administer the water that we have said for the cure of the abscesses caused by the mother.
And if there occurs a flow of blood, then send them down to styptic waters and administer the other cure.
And I have already seen a woman in whose belly was a dead fetus, and then over that fire another pregnancy, and then over the dead fetus, another. It happened to me a long time ago an abscess in the navel; and it inflated so that a fire opened, and it began to throw out pus.
And I was called to the cure of it, and medicated it for a long time, and the plague did not consolidate.
Then I placed on it some causes of plaster of strong attraction, and extracted from it a bone, and after a few days passed, and extracted another bone; and I was too amazed, as in the belly there were no bones.
And then I thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
Therefore I continued to treat the abscess, and extracted from it more bones, the woman existing in her usual dispositions, and already living in that manner for a long time, cured of it a little pus.
And I do not affirm that it is strange, but that in this there is science and help to what the physician artifices with his hand for cure administers.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of the verge with which the mother is opened:
This is the form of the stretcher in which the blades are inserted, to which insertion there are two verges in two extremities of two feet. But however this verge must be more subtle of strictor, and be made either of ebony or of wood of boys.
And its width of each shaft is two fingers and the margin of each is one finger, and the length of each is one palm and a half; and in the middle place of the two shafts there are two adjustments of that same shaft, which are already fastened, of which the length is the majority of one palm and a little less, and the width of each is two fingers, or a little less.
And these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the mother so that it be opened with those when you revolve the two prescribed verges.
Other form similar to that more subtle and lighter:
It is made of ebony or wood shafts according to the likeness of forceps. But however at the extremity of it there are two additions as it were, and the length of those additions is as one palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And as you want with those to open the mother, then you make the woman lie on the sheet with her feet dangling, open what is between her thighs. And then open your hand with the instrument as you do with forceps, according to the amount that you want of the opening of the mouth of the mother until the midwife makes it so that you want.
