Of extraction of the secondine.
When the secondine is retained in childbirth, then it is necessary that you command the patient to retain her breath, and then make that stir with condition, and strengthen your hand over the mouth of it and over the nostrils of it, and if by this it is brought out, well is.
And if not, then you take a wool and perforate in the cover a hole and place in that herbs burning the mouth of the mother, as well as  calament and rue and anise and chamomile and sicados arabic and cinnamon and centaury. All these herbs or some of them are submerged in water in the wool, and place that over the fire.
And then place a tube of cane in the mouth of the mother, and keep that inside that the vapor comes to the cavity of the mother.
And then make that stir as we have said, and the secondine is thrown out with velocity.
But if remain after this cure and it is not brought out, then you command the midwife to submerge her left hand in sesame oil or in a mixture of althea, and then introduce that into the cone and caress with that the secondine, and as that is found, then take it and extend it little by little. But if it is annexed in the perineum of the mother, then introduce her hand as we have recounted, and when she will have found the secondine, extract it little by little according to rectum so that the mother does not feel the traction vehement. Lift so that it be changed to the right and left sides with ease.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted, we have already recounted the cure with stir and with medication of the wool with herbs.
But if it is not thrown out with all the causes which we have recounted, then guard that you do not fatigue over that in iteration of abstraction, but rather that what is brought out of it to the mouth of the mother lies to the cloth of the woman, and then sterilize that with enguent and tetrafarmacon; for that will make it rot that near some days and will be dissolved and will be thrown out.
But when it may be possible, it is of it elevated bad odor to the head, and to the stomach, and that ledeys the patient; and then it is necessary that sub-fumigations and conveniences be administered to it.
But some of the Ancients already are proven sub-fumigation of nazitort and of figs dried.
Form of instrument with which the woman is sub-fumigated ofves the retention of menstruation and of the secondine:
It is made of wire or of brass.
And it is placed the subtle extremity in the cone and the wide extremity over the fire, and the sub-fumigation is placed over the embers of the fire.
And keep that inside that the sub-fumigation be consumed and iterate another.
Of cure of the anus of the unperforated child.
Many children are born and the anuses of them are not perforated, those which already have a subtle and opilated. Therefore it is necessary to the midwife that with her finger she perforates that cicatricle; and if not, perforate that with a sharp spatula, and guard that it does not touch the lacert.
And then place over that wool infused in wine and oil; and then cure that with enguent inside that it is senat.
But if you fear that it is opilated, then place in the hole a tube for many days, and remove it when the child will want to defecate.
And already accidies opilation of the anus by consolidation of plague or of abscess; therefore it is necessary that that consolidation be incised, and then it be cured with that which we have said of the cure and of the lead.
Of cure of the fistulas that become from below.
The fistulas that become in the part below pus low and nodulation and thickness which become near the anus outside or in the space of the one part.
And it is a fistula or ulcers.
And because that node is antiquated and runs from the moist white humidity or subtle pus, and sometimes from these fistulas some penetrate.
And those that penetrate are known by what is emitted from them by the egress and by windiness; and sometimes the patient uses the egress, and very often it is emitted from these worms.
And sometimes from these fistulas, in the space, they penetrate into the bladder, and into the meat of the vagina; and sometimes from these they penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the knot of the hip.
And in which it is known that a fistula penetrates into the anus and does not penetrate, is that you put your finger inside the anus, and you introduce a subtle probe of thread or iron into the fistula when there is no turgescence.
But if there is turgescence, then introduce into that a subtle probe of lead or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair in your finger.
And if you do not feel that at all, nor do you process from the tract any cause of egress or worms or windiness, thus as we have said, then you know that it is not penetrating, and then you turn to the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the meat of the vagina, then the signification of it is the emission of urine from that and prohibition of it so that the place with medicine may be consolidated.
But if it is penetrating into the joint of the thigh or into the hip and causing pain in the circuit, then the sign of it is that the probe penetrates here if there is no turgescence into the hip, and causing pain in the circuit of the part; and that from it pus is always yielded; and that it does not work in that medication, nor is it consolidated with an enema.
And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no cure of all, and the cure of those is the work and vanity of the physicians' leaves upon which they are founded.
But in that which is not penetrating and not antiquated, healing with iron is expected according to what I have told you, and what I have already tried and proven.
And it is that the patient lies between your hands on their two sides and elevates their legs onto them, the thighs being inclined to the belly of them, and then introduce a probe of lead, or thread if there is turgescence in the fistula, until you know the place where the probe penetrates.
And if that feels the patient around the buttock, then cover that when you introduce your finger into the buttock.
And if you feel in your finger the probe already by itself penetrating, or another thing that you feel between your finger and that skin or flesh, then you know certainly that that is penetrating; and therefore do not work on that, for it is not in that healing, as we have said.
But however, some say that it is healed in some men tart.
And of the medication by which is expected help in it is that you ignite a subtle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as it is preceded, and introduce that ignited into the fistula until it reaches around the buttock; and then repeat that two or three times until you know that all those fleshy parts adjusted to the fistula have been cauterized, which are like the quill of a bird's feather.
And then cure that with poultices wrapped in border until all those fleshy parts that have been cauterized can be covered, and then cure that with medicines that engender and consolidate the flesh, and if it is healed, well is; and if not, then it is not healed in any time by other cure.
And if the probe enters, and does not penetrate into your finger which is in the buttock, and between that and the probe which is veiled by flesh or skin, and sometimes the fistula in that which seizes the surface of the pudendum, then dry the pudendum from the beginning of the fistula, and you see drying by the probe, and in the fistula until the drying reaches the place where the extremity of the probe reaches, and by the probe is liberated and catched.
And then purify those fistulous fleshy parts which are assembled to the quill of a bird's feather and do not break from those any cause.
But if flux of blood sometimes comes between you and your operation when you were inserting those fleshy parts, then the best that may be and of the light pus instrument is to cauterize with fire or with acute medicine, for cauterizing with fire adjusts good two habits: it is the cauterization of those fleshy parts adjusted, and abscess of the blood and excretion of the humidities.
And then cure that with poultices wrapped in border or in cauterized tripe until the place gets brace, and then cure the plague with enemas of flesh-hardening and consolidating.
And so medicines in which there is astringency and excretion; when then it is restored it is already healed and you do not fear iteration.
But if the fistula already reaches into the preon of the buttock and is elongated from it to the surface of the body, then introduce your finger into the buttock and inquire with that.
And therefore if you feel the probe and between you and it is veiled by skin or flesh, and it is proper to penetration, then there is no operation in it but according to the way of trust and of hope.
This cause is administered in him in one of three ways: either that cauterize that as we have said; or that succeeds that within that you can achieve the concavity of him so that it is possible to you to intervene the qualcas and the cure propdana; and do not process mot am seccio so that no incides le lacert containing le cuol, and that accidisque over the malaute eyssiment of the egistio ses voluntat; and then cure that am that we have said quar fort leu sira sanat; or that elongues that velament and mondes that pus that seccas that within prop le cul, as we have said, or am tenta or am another instrument of acute extremitat, and aprop mondifique those carns fistuladas the ones that so in the seccio entro the one podes am percrustacio; and aprop esforsa te to far la restauracio of tota la plagua am seccio, and if the orrifici pus desus is not consolidated, and romangua the fistula uberta in the partida del cul, and sira pus leugier per le malaute. And do this to all, and leave one of them uncooked, so that the superfluity of blood runs from that one.
And place on the buttocks a cloth soaked in rose oil or in cerot; and place that on the buttocks and command the patient to rest. And then leave that inside the box; and when it is dried, cure those with ointment or with another cure inside the box.
And since they are old and do not heal in this medicine, then when you have those with the point of a spatula or with your fingernail, while they are made moist and are hosted by the pus that flows from them, which prevents them from consolidating; and then cure them when they are consolidated.

Know that almesamir, it is called, and is not if not a red knot according to the color of the body resembling a head of a clavicle, and it is made in all the body and mostly in the parts below the feet and at the knees, and therefore by those pains you must know the ailment.
And therefore when it is incised that which is in the circuit of the claw, and it is held with the forceps or with an anvil, and it is eradicated from its root; and then cure that.
And if you want, cauterize the following as it is preceded in its chapter.
But of the wart is a small eminence rough fistulated round on the surface of the body, and many times they come in the most of the children.
And the cure of it is that you extend and cut that, or that you tighten that with a thread or with a pellet inside a box. And if you want, cauterize that, as we have said, with fire or with acute medicine.
But a formica is a small eminence,  feutrada or fistulated thick on the surface of the body, going to the groin, and when the ant touches it, it is felt in it resembling a bite of an ant, and it is made around the body.
And the cure of it is that you take a quill of eagle or of vulture, and it be strong, and place that on the formica while it contains the circle of the quill of the parts of it; and then revolve your hand with the quill while you cut that which is in the circuit of the formica, and place that in the groin of the flesh, and that you eradicate the formica from its root.
And if you want, do this with a quill of iron or of steel according to this form:

And if you want, cauterize the formica according to what is said before in the cauterization of atheyl in the chapter of cauteries.
Of the form of the instruments that are administered to give christening.
Sometimes christening is done with silver or with lead or with iron melted or malleated; and sometimes it is done with those instruments small and large according to those to whom they are administered, that which is administered in the cure of the small children be small; and of those whose buttocks are rough or painful, the christenings of those be small.
The form of the large and few christening:
The head of the quill of it from above in which the pouch is tied be wide according to this manner; and be to it distinction the one where the pouch is tied as it is sometimes.
And the extremity of it from below, which is inserted into the anus, be dull (so it is not open) much lion, drawing to subtlety; and in one of the sides of it be two holes, and on the other side one hole, and be the width of the hole according to the thickness of the rays and a little thicker.
And be the pouch in which are placed the medicines of bladder of beast or of sheepskin, and the root of it be a palm.
And be perforated by many holes as it is revolved; and if the space which is between the holes the thickness of the finger.
And then insert into those holes a strong thread of cru thread which be of ten threads, or about those; and adjust with that the pouch; and when it is placed in it the pouch, be straight in the head of the christening between two distinct ones with strong constriction, and then christenize with that each hole: But the quality of christenizing with that is that you fill the pouch with the medicine, that it be warmed according to the quantity of the tolerance of the patient; and guard yourself that it be not too hot nor too cold.
And then the patient be laid on his back, and raise his legs up and place below him a cushion on which already are the men or a bolster; and then anoint the extremity of the cautery with oil or with album of hen or with mucellage of fenugrec or of similar; and then insert that into the anus with facility, and then the minister grasps the pouch and expresses that with two hands and at the same time with vehemence until it be evacuated into the bowel all that which is in the christening; and then extract the christening and the patient lifts his legs to the wall.
And if the medicine forces him to vomit, he should have as much as he can; and if he sleeps with it all night, it is more beneficial.
But if you treat him for diseases of the solution of the belly and his vomiting, then you iterate the cautery while it is healing.
And if in the anus there are hemorrhoids or festering abscesses, then be the cautery very subtle and lion, of the cauteries with which the children are cauterized.
Of the cure of plagues.
And I have already said in the division of the cure of plagues what was convenient to the book, and I say so the cure of those with my and medicines according to the complement.
Therefore I say that the plagues are diversified according to what by which the plagues are made and according to the place upon which the plagues fall.
And the causes for which many times the plagues are made are such as a bite of a viper, or incision of a sword or of a dagger, or percussion with a lance, or with a club, or with an arrow, or similar to those of many causes.
But the plagues that are in the places of the body are such as a plague which falls upon the head, or the neck, or the feet, or the belly, or the arm, and similar to those of the limbs.
And I am recounting the cure of some plagues so that you pause that reasoning and rule over the other plagues.
And I begin with the plagues of the head simple, for the remembrance of the composite will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore I say that when a simple plague occurs in the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is by a bite of a viper or similar, and the wound has already been cleansed alone and it is a great plague and fears about that patient having an abscess, then you cauterize and perform cephalic phlebotomy immediately, and do not delay this; and extract from that of the blood according to the quantity of its virtue if no other cause prohibits phlebotomy, especially if the blood that is emitted from the plague is little.
And be the phlebotomy on the opposite side of the afflicted area; and guard the patient from repletion and from wine and from coarse food.
But if from the minutia any cause prohibits, then let the food be lessened and do not approach to meat nor to wine.
And place on the plague, if to it there occurs an abscess cauterize, coat infused in rose oil or in wine in which it is steeped.
But if it is certain of an abscess cauterize, then place on the plague, if it is recent with its blood and the air has not changed that the powder which I will recount shortly.
And if the air has already changed that, then place on the wound until it is healed.
But if the plague is great or is by incision of a sword and similar, and the lips of it are not adjusted by pessaries, then adjust those with suture according to that I will recount of the suture of them.
But if the plague is already discovered of the bone and skin, and there is no retention of it but a small suspensory, then incise that and apply to the plague with medicines and restore the flesh to the place of the wound, and command the patient to be cautious of foods in which there is grossness: caps and forms cooked meat and similar to them, until it is composed.
And if there is a putrefaction in the wound and it does not adhere to the bone, then you incise all that and throw it away, and then cure that.
But if in these plagues an artery or vein is present from which blood can flow, and it is not incised by medicines, then you inquire about the artery, and if you find that it is not incised, then you incise that with a spatula, or lick that; and if necessity provokes that what we have said does not confer, then you cauterize until the blood is stopped.
And if these plagues are simple and small, then the cause of them is light; so that you pulverize over those this powder, because it consolidates before the air changes them.
And the manner of the powder is this: take olive oil, one part, of dragon's blood, two parts, of cauterized earth, three parts; be all three ground and sifted, and of it be the wound filled, and be constricted by good constriction until it well adheres over that, and be coagulated with the blood.
And after strengthens that with pessaries and leaves it, and do not untie it while it is so that it is not apostematized, for no medicine is extracted from it until it is healed.
And sometimes do this alone cauterize, when it is not to you in present olive oil and dragon's blood.
And already do this same operation in the great plagues when it is necessary that it be placed over them and be tightened, and are recent plagues with their blood, those which the air has not altered.

Of the wounds of the belly.

And know that the suture of the belly is done in four ways, but two sutures are common that are used in sutures of the other wounds of the body.
And two other sutures proper are used in the others, but they are more proper in the suture of the belly.
And I recommend to you each one with exposition and explanation.
Therefore I say that when the wound is small and there is some cause of the hernia through that, and it is difficult to reduce that, then it is done in one of two ways: or by the smallness of the incision as we have said, or when the hernia has come inflammation because of the cold of the air.
And therefore when this is so, then you should poultice that, immersing a sponge or cloth wet in tepid water, or which you have boiled in water with squill, and cypress, and spikenard, and apply that to the hernia until the inflammation is resolved.
And sometimes do this with wine which has astringency, and it is better than water alone in the resolution of the inflammation.
And therefore when you see the inflammation being resolved, then you moisten the hernia with water in which are boiled alder and mallows, for by this it is alleviated the pain of it with little cause.
But if the pain of it is excused with this cure, then widen the incision a little with an instrument with which hemorrhoids are incised.

Of the instrument, this is the form of it:
One part of it is sharp, and the other part is not sharp, and the tip is subtle, and not as subtle as a spatula, but blunt a little.

And similarly if the incision is in one of the two parts of the belly, then place your understanding and your consideration always in that way so that the part in which the wound is is higher than the other.
And thus it is necessary that you administer this in the large wounds and in the middle wounds.
And in the small wounds, place that which is prepared by you, and make that it be ministered between your fingers, which has the incision all with its hand and adjusts the lips of it, and then uncover from that to that which you see the suture any cause to another.
And this is the common way of suturing: one that you take the needle, or count of needles according to the quantity of the width of the wound; and then lay it from the end of the incision of the ring finger, and strengthen the needle one, or another that you do not put thread in the two extremities of the cord, with two extremities of the  ciph, which is below the cord of the parts of the fingers, until you make it penetrate from that part; and you have already joined two extremities of the cord and two extremities of the ciph, and are made four orders.
And then strengthen with thread double in the circuit of the needle, and sometimes of two parts at once, and then join the two lips and the wound by decent joining; and then lay the thickness of the finger and fix another needle in that, and then tie that with thread as you tied with the first needle; and do not cease to do this if it is necessary with the needles until you have completed the whole constriction of the wound.
And let the needles be medium between thickness and subtlety, because the subtle needles slightly cut the flesh; and the thick ones are difficult to enter into the cord, and therefore for that reason they should be medium in subtlety and thickness.
And do not let the needle be fixed in two extremities of the cord properly, so that the flesh is not slightly cut and that the wound may be healed before its consolidation.
And do not be prolonged in suturing so that the wound may be hindered from consolidation.
And then cut the extremities of the needles so that they do not prick the patient's sleep; and place on the suture powders expanded of all parts, which have the extremities of the needles; and leave those until you know that the wound is already consolidated.
And these kinds of suturing with needles in this way is most convenient in the small wounds, because it suffices in the suturing of them one needle or two or around those.
But the second suturing is common: and it is that you administer with suturing the four extremities, of the cord and two extremities of the ciph, in one time, with a needle in which the thread is enveloped equal in subtlety and thickness.
And when you have penetrated these four extremities with the needle, reduce the needle from that same part from which you began, so that the thread retracted is taken from the higher part to the wound, so that the suture is like a suture of cloth with which the cloths are tightened.
And pause between each suture the quantity of the thickness of the little finger.
And this suture is for men.

Of the cure of zuech and fistula.
Know that every plague and abscess when it is inflamed and becomes old, and it is made an ulcer, and it is not consolidated and sweats all the time and is not cut off, then, in whatever member it may be, universally it is called a fistula and we call that azukem.
And fistula according to truth is a fetid, hard, white knot, with which there is no pain and to which the cavity is like the cavity of a bird's bone; and for this reason that one is called alcus rizatz, that is, bone.
And it is in some men humid, the one which sweats; and very soon the humidity is cut off in some hours. And some times this humidity is much, and is little, and is thick, and is subtle.
I have already shown all those causes, the signs of them, and the cure of them with medicines in the division.
And I will tell you how to cure a fistula which is made by operation with a knife.
And know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for some of them reach the large veins and arteries, or the nerves, or the head, or the intestines, or the bladder, or any of the ribs, or any of the vertebrae of the spine, or any of the joints composed by composition, as between the hand and foot; and of these, some give rise to proximity to the principal member and its counterparts.
And therefore of these fistulas that are of this manner, those are of the diseases of difficult healing, and do not receive cure, and occupation with them is work and ignorance.
And if it is of the fistulas any one the depth of which does not reach those places that have been said, and you wait and confide in the cure of it, and you want to arrive at knowledge of it, then take a probe or a piece of iron, and if the fistula goes straight, and inquire about it with it.
But if the fistula is tortuous, then investigate it with a probe of fine lead, because lead with the lightness of its body is eased and curved of its tortuosity.
And if the fistula is having many horrible things, it is not possible for you to signify upon it with a probe.
Therefore, irrigate the orifice with its orifices, because the moisture by which you irrigate it should go to the other orifices and run from them.
And then inquire exquisitely, according to what manner it is possible for you to know if here has bone or nerve, and if the concavity of the fistula is distant or proximate, or if it is a fistula to which there are many orifices and this above all with the sum of your strength, with your interrogation, with which you interrogate the patient, and the invention of the pain you derive your compression with the hand over the area, and similarities of the significations and causes accidental to the abscess.
And since you have stood upon all those causes with true station, then come to the cure according to confidence: and it is that you consider then if the fistula is apparent proximate or in a salty place, distant from a joint, or from a nerve, or from an artery, or from a vein, or from one of the places which I have told you.
Then you dry the fistula according to what has been said before of the narration of it, and remove what is in that filtration and of corrupted flesh, and what is born in the orifice of the flesh, or of the veil and of similarities, and cure that while it is healing.
But if the fistula is of distant depth, and is straight, then you must cut that into the preon as much as you are able, and then modify that of all its corrupted flesh; and then administer poultices wrapped in acute medicines, and introduce those into the concavity of the fistula, which you have understood with iron.

And then restore that with unguents which generate healthy flesh until it is healed.

And if it is not healed and throws back as it was doing, then you know that you have not arrived at the total eradication of the corruption; and therefore you uncover it again and exquisitely make the root and purification of it with the rearmost strength of your own, and then restore that.

Of extraction of arrows.
